Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Utah Workforce Services Code
==============================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 1 - Department of Workforce Services
******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This title is known as the "Utah Workforce Services Code."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Unless otherwise specified, as used in this title:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(1): Chapter 3, Employment Support Act; Chapter 5, Training and Workforce Improvement Act "Client" means an individual who the department has determined to be eligible for services or benefits under:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(1)(a): Chapter 3, Employment Support Act
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(1)(b): Chapter 5, Training and Workforce Improvement Act
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(2): 35A-1-103 "Department" means the Department of Workforce Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(3): Chapter 2, Economic Service Areas "Economic service area" means an economic service area established in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(4): Chapter 3, Employment Support Act; Chapter 5, Training and Workforce Improvement Act "Employment assistance" means services or benefits provided by the department under:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(4)(a): Chapter 3, Employment Support Act
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(4)(b): Chapter 5, Training and Workforce Improvement Act
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(5): 35A-2-201 "Employment center" is a location in an economic service area where the services provided by an economic service area under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(6): Chapter 2, Economic Service Areas "Employment counselor" means an individual responsible for developing an employment plan and coordinating the services and benefits under this title in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(7): "Employment plan" means a written agreement between the department and a client that describes:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(7)(a): the relationship between the department and the client;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(7)(b): the obligations of the department and the client; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(7)(c): the result if an obligation is not fulfilled by the department or the client.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(8): 35A-1-201 "Executive director" means the executive director of the department appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(9): 53B-2-101; 53G-7-401 "Government entity" means the state or any county, municipality, special district, special service district, or other political subdivision or administrative unit of the state, a state institution of higher education as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(10): Chapter 3, Employment Support Act; Title 26B, Chapter 3, Health Care - Administration and Assistance "Public assistance" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(10)(a): Chapter 3, Employment Support Act services or benefits provided under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(10)(b): Title 26B, Chapter 3, Health Care - Administration and Assistance medical assistance provided under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(10)(c): foster care maintenance payments provided from the General Fund or under Title IV-E of the Social Security Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(10)(d): SNAP benefits; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(10)(e): any other public funds expended for the benefit of a person in need of financial, medical, food, housing, or related assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(11): "SNAP" means the federal "Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program" under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(12): "SNAP benefit" or "SNAP benefits" means a financial benefit, coupon, or privilege available under SNAP.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(13): "Stabilization" means addressing the basic living, family care, and social or psychological needs of the client so that the client may take advantage of training or employment opportunities provided under this title or through other agencies or institutions.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(14): "Vulnerable populations" means children or adults with a life situation that substantially affects that individual's ability to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(14)(a): provide personal protection;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(14)(b): provide necessities such as food, shelter, clothing, or mental or other health care;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(14)(c): obtain services necessary for health, safety, or welfare;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(14)(d): carry out the activities of daily living;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(14)(e): manage the adult's own financial resources; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-102(14)(f): comprehend the nature and consequences of remaining in a situation of abuse, neglect, or exploitation.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-103 Department of Workforce Services -- Creation -- Seal.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-103(1): There is created the Department of Workforce Services, which has all of the policymaking functions, regulatory and enforcement powers, rights, duties, and responsibilities outlined in this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-103(2): For purposes of this title, the department shall have an official seal that shall be judicially noticed.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104 Department authority.
-----------------------------------------------------
Within all other authority or responsibility granted to it by law, the department may:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act adopt rules when authorized by this title, in accordance with the procedures of
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(2): purchase, as authorized or required by law, services that the department is responsible to provide for legally eligible persons;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(3): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act conduct adjudicative proceedings in accordance with the procedures of
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(4): establish eligibility standards for department programs, not inconsistent with state or federal law or regulations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(5): take necessary steps, including legal action, to recover money or the monetary value of services provided to a recipient who is not eligible;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(6): administer oaths, certify to official acts, issue subpoenas to compel witnesses and the production of books, accounts, documents, and other records necessary as evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(7): acquire, manage, and dispose of any real or personal property needed or owned by the department, not inconsistent with state law;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(8): receive gifts, grants, devises, and donations or their proceeds, crediting the program designated by the donor, and using the gift, grant, devise, or donation for the purposes requested by the donor, as long as the request conforms to state and federal policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(9): accept and employ volunteer labor or services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(10): reimburse volunteers for necessary expenses, when the department considers that reimbursement to be appropriate;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(11): carry out the responsibility assigned by the State Workforce Services Plan developed by the State Workforce Development Board;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(12): (12)(a); Title 63G, Chapter 22, State Training and Certification Requirements
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(12)(a): provide training and educational opportunities for the department's staff; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(12)(b): (12)(a); Title 63G, Chapter 22, State Training and Certification Requirements ensure that any training or educational opportunity described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(13): examine and audit the expenditures of any public funds provided to a local authority, agency, or organization that contracts with or receives funds from those authorities or agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(14): accept and administer grants from the federal government and from other sources, public or private;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(15): employ and determine the compensation of clerical, legal, technical, investigative, and other employees necessary to carry out the department's policymaking, regulatory, and enforcement powers, rights, duties, and responsibilities under this title;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(16): establish and conduct free employment agencies, and bring together employers seeking employees and working people seeking employment, and make known the opportunities for employment in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(17): collect, collate, and publish statistical and other information relating to employees, employers, employments, and places of employment, and other statistics as the department considers proper;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(18): encourage the expansion and use of apprenticeship programs meeting state or federal standards for apprenticeship programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(19): develop processes to ensure that the department responds to the full range of employee and employer clients; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104(20): carry out the responsibilities assigned to the department by statute.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104.5 Other department duties -- Strategic plan for health system reform -- Reporting suspected misuse of a Social Security number.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104.5(1): The department shall work with the Department of Health, the Insurance Department, the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity, and the Legislature to develop the health system reform.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104.5(2): In the process of determining an individual's eligibility for a public benefit or service under this title or under federal law, if the department determines that a valid social security number is being used by an unauthorized individual, the department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104.5(2)(a): inform the individual who the department determines to be the likely actual owner of the social security number or, if the likely actual owner is a minor, the minor's parent or guardian, of the suspected misuse; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104.5(2)(b): subject to federal law, provide information of the suspected misuse to an appropriate law enforcement agency responsible for investigating identity fraud.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-104.5(3): (2)(b) If the department learns or determines that providing information under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-105 Department budget -- Reports from divisions.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-105(1): The department shall prepare and submit to the governor for inclusion in the governor's budget to be submitted to the Legislature, a budget of the department's financial requirements needed to carry out its responsibilities as provided by law during the fiscal year following the Legislature's next annual general session.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-105(2): The executive director shall require a report from each of the divisions and offices of the department, to aid in preparation of the departmental budget.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-106 Fees.
-------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-106(1): 63J-1-504 Unless otherwise provided by statute, the department may adopt a schedule of fees assessed for services provided by the department by following the procedures and requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-106(2): The department shall submit each fee established under this section to the Legislature for its approval as part of the department's annual appropriations request.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109 Annual report -- Content -- Format.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(1): The department shall prepare and submit to the governor and the Legislature, by October 1 of each year, an annual written report of the operations, activities, programs, and services of the department, including its divisions, offices, boards, commissions, councils, and committees, for the preceding fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2): (2)(b); (c) For each operation, activity, program, or service provided by the department, the annual report shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(a): a description of the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(b): data and metrics:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(b)(i): selected and used by the department to measure progress, performance, effectiveness, and scope of the operation, activity, program, or service, including summary data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(b)(ii): that are consistent and comparable for each state operation, activity, program, or service that primarily involves employment training or placement as determined by the executive director, the commissioner of higher education, and the executive director of the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(c): budget data, including the amount and source of funding, expenses, and allocation of full-time employees for the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(d): (2)(b); (c) historical data from previous years for comparison with data reported under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(e): goals, challenges, and achievements related to the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(f): relevant federal and state statutory references and requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(g): contact information of officials knowledgeable and responsible for each operation, activity, program, or service; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(h): other information determined by the department that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(h)(i): may be needed, useful, or of historical significance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(2)(h)(ii): promotes accountability and transparency for each operation, activity, program, or service with the public and elected officials.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(3): The annual report shall be designed to provide clear, accurate, and accessible information to the public, the governor, and the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(4): 68-3-14; (2)(b); 53B-34-102 The department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(4)(a): 68-3-14 submit the annual report in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(4)(b): make the annual report, and previous annual reports, accessible to the public by placing a link to the reports on the department's website; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-109(4)(c): (2)(b); 53B-34-102 provide the data and metrics described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201 Executive director -- Appointment -- Removal -- Compensation -- Qualifications -- Responsibilities -- Deputy directors.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(1): Title 67, Chapter 22, State Officer Compensation
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(1)(a): The chief administrative officer of the department is the executive director, who is appointed by the governor with the advice and consent of the Senate.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(1)(b): The executive director serves at the pleasure of the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(1)(c): Title 67, Chapter 22, State Officer Compensation The executive director shall receive a salary established by the governor within the salary range fixed by the Legislature in
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(1)(d): The executive director shall be experienced in administration, management, and coordination of complex organizations.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(2): Title 63A, Chapter 17, Utah State Personnel Management Act; Chapter 2, Economic Service Areas; 35A-1-109(2)(b) The executive director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(2)(a): Title 63A, Chapter 17, Utah State Personnel Management Act administer and supervise the department in compliance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(2)(b): Chapter 2, Economic Service Areas supervise and coordinate between the economic service areas and directors created under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(2)(c): coordinate policies and program activities conducted through the divisions and economic service areas of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(2)(d): approve the proposed budget of each division, the Workforce Appeals Board, and each economic service area within the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(2)(e): approve all applications for federal grants or assistance in support of any department program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(2)(f): 35A-1-109(2)(b) coordinate with the executive directors of the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity and the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget to review data and metrics to be reported to the Legislature as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(2)(g): fulfill such other duties as assigned by the Legislature or as assigned by the governor that are not inconsistent with this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(3): The executive director may appoint deputy or assistant directors to assist the executive director in carrying out the department's responsibilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-201(4): The executive director shall at least annually provide for the sharing of information between the advisory councils established under this title.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203 Executive director -- Jurisdiction over division and economic service area directors -- No jurisdiction over Workforce Appeals Board -- Authority.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(1): The executive director has administrative jurisdiction over each division and economic service area.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(2): To effectuate greater statewide efficiency and local flexibility in the implementation of programs, the executive director shall coordinate with the directors of the divisions and the directors of the economic service areas.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(3): To effectuate greater efficiency and economy in the operations of the department, the executive director may:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(3)(a): make changes in personnel and service functions in the divisions and economic service areas under the executive director's administrative jurisdiction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(3)(b): authorize designees to perform appropriate responsibilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(4): (4)(b); 35A-1-303
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(4)(a): (4)(b) The executive director has no jurisdiction over the Workforce Appeals Board except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(4)(b): 35A-1-303 The executive director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(4)(b)(i): approve the budget of the Workforce Appeals Board;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(4)(b)(ii): provide the necessary staff support to the Workforce Appeals Board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(4)(b)(iii): 35A-1-303 make rules necessary for the operations of the Workforce Appeals Board and the efficiency of the adjudicative process as a whole in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-203(5): To facilitate management of the department, the executive director may establish offices necessary to implement this title or to perform functions such as budgeting, planning, data processing, and personnel administration.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205 Workforce Appeals Board -- Chair -- Appointment -- Compensation -- Qualifications.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(1): There is created the Workforce Appeals Board within the department consisting of one or more panels to hear and decide appeals from the decision of an administrative law judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(2): (5)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(2)(a): (5) A panel shall consist of three impartial members appointed by the governor as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(2)(a)(i): (5) the board chair, appointed in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(2)(a)(ii): one member appointed to represent employers; and in making this appointment, the governor shall consider nominations from employer organizations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(2)(a)(iii): one member appointed to represent employees; and in making this appointment, the governor shall consider nominations from employee organizations.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(2)(b): No more than two members of a panel may belong to the same political party.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(3): (3)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(3)(a): (3)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(3)(a)(i): (3)(a)(ii) The term of a member shall be six years beginning on March 1 of the year the member is appointed, except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(3)(a)(ii): The governor shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of members are staggered so that approximately one third of the members are appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(3)(b): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(3)(c): The governor may remove a member for inefficiency, neglect of duty, malfeasance or misfeasance in office, or other good and sufficient cause.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(3)(d): A member shall hold office until a successor is appointed and has qualified.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(4): (4)(b); 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; (5); Title 63A, Chapter 17, Utah State Personnel Management Act
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(4)(a): (4)(b); 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(4)(a)(i): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(4)(a)(ii): 63A-3-107 Section

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(4)(b): (5); Title 63A, Chapter 17, Utah State Personnel Management Act The member appointed as board chair in accordance with Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(5)(a): The chief officer of the board shall be the chair, who shall serve as the executive and administrative head of the board.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(5)(c): The chair shall be experienced in administration and possess any additional qualifications determined by the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(6)(a): The chair shall designate an alternate from a panel appointed under this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(6)(a)(i): in the absence of a regular member or the chair; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(6)(a)(ii): if the regular member or the chair has a conflict of interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(6)(b): Each case shall be decided by a full three-member panel.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-205(7): The department shall provide the Workforce Appeals Board necessary staff support, except, the board may employ, retain, or appoint legal counsel.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206 State Workforce Development Board -- Appointment -- Membership -- Terms of members -- Compensation.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(1): There is created within the department the State Workforce Development Board in accordance with the provisions of the Workforce Innovation and Opportunity Act, 29 U.S.C.  Sec. 3101 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2): The board shall consist of the following 38 members:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(a): the governor or the governor's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(b): one member of the Senate, appointed by the president of the Senate;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(c): one representative of the House of Representatives, appointed by the speaker of the House of Representatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(d): the executive director or the executive director's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(e): the executive director of the Department of Human Services or the executive director's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(f): the director of the Utah State Office of Rehabilitation or the director's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(g): the state superintendent of public instruction or the superintendent's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(h): the commissioner of higher education or the commissioner's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(i): the executive director of the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity or the executive director's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(j): the executive director of the Department of Veterans and Military Affairs or the executive director's designee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k): the following members appointed by the governor:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(i): 20 representatives of business in the state, selected among the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(i)(A): owners of businesses, chief executive or operating officers of businesses, or other business executives or employers with policymaking or hiring authority;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(i)(B): representatives of businesses, including small businesses, that provide employment opportunities that include high-quality, work-relevant training and development in in-demand industry sectors or occupations in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(i)(C): representatives of businesses appointed from among individuals nominated by state business organizations or business trade associations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(ii): six representatives of the workforce within the state, which:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(ii)(A): shall include at least two representatives of labor organizations who have been nominated by state labor federations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(ii)(B): shall include at least one representative from a registered apprentice program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(ii)(C): may include one or more representatives from a community-based organization that has demonstrated experience and expertise in addressing the employment, training, or educational needs of individuals with barriers to employment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(ii)(D): may include one or more representatives from an organization that has demonstrated experience and expertise in addressing the employment, training, or education needs of eligible youth, including organizations that serve out of school youth; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(2)(k)(iii): two elected officials that represent a city or a county.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(3)(a): The governor shall appoint one of the appointed business representatives as chair of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(3)(b): The chair shall serve at the pleasure of the governor.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(4)(b): A member appointed by the governor shall serve a term of four years and may be reappointed to one additional term.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-206(4)(c): A member shall continue to serve until the member's successor has been appointed and qualified.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207 State workforce services plan -- Economic service area plans.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The State Workforce Development Board shall annually maintain and update a state workforce services plan that includes:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(1): a four-year strategy, as described in 29 U.S.C. Sec. 3112, for the following core programs:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(1)(a): youth services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(1)(b): adult employment and training services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(1)(c): dislocated worker employment and training services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(1)(d): adult education and literacy activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(1)(e): employment services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(1)(f): vocational rehabilitation services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(2): a strategy for aligning and coordinating the core programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(3): a strategy for coordinating the workforce needs of job seekers and employers in the various regions of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(4): planning to ensure that employment centers address the requirements of the special employment needs population, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(4)(a): individuals who have special employment needs based on factors such as race, gender, age, disability, economic status, education, language skills, or work history; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(4)(b): an "individual with a barrier to employment" as that term is defined in 29 U.S.C. Sec. 3102;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(5): a mechanism for getting consumer and public feedback on department programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(6): projected analysis of the workforce needs of employers and clients;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(7): state outcome-based standards for measuring program performance to ensure equitable service to all clients;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(8): strategies to ensure program responsiveness, universal access, and unified case management;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(9): strategies to eliminate unnecessary barriers to access services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-207(10): strategies to provide assistance to employees facing employment dislocation and their employers.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-302 Review of administrative order -- Finality of Workforce Appeals Board's order.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-302(1): An order entered by an administrative law judge under this title is the final decision of the department unless a further appeal is initiated under this title and in accordance with the rules of the department governing the review.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-302(2): The order of the Workforce Appeals Board on review is final, unless set aside by the court of appeals.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-302(3): If an order is appealed to the court of appeals after the party appealing the order has exhausted all administrative appeals, the court of appeals has jurisdiction to review, reverse, or annul any order of the Workforce Appeals Board, or to suspend or delay the operation or execution of the order of the Workforce Appeals Board being appealed.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-303 Rulemaking.
-------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-303(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-303(1)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-303(1)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act Except as provided in this title and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-303(2): The rules made under this section shall include procedures to dispose of cases informally, or to expedite claims adjudication, narrow issues, and simplify the methods of proof at hearings.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-303(3): Any rule made concerning proceedings before the Workforce Appeals Board shall be made in consultation with the Workforce Appeals Board.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304 Review authority of the Workforce Appeals Board.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(1)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act In accordance with this title and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(1)(b): An appeal filed by the party shall be allowed as of right if the decision of the administrative law judge did not affirm the department's prior decision.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(1)(c): If the Workforce Appeals Board denies an application for appeal from the decision of an administrative law judge, the decision of the administrative law judge is considered a decision of the Workforce Appeals Board for purposes of judicial review and is subject to judicial review if further appeal is initiated under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(2): On appeal, the Workforce Appeals Board may on the basis of the evidence previously submitted in the case, or upon the basis of any additional evidence it requires:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(2)(a): affirm the decision of the administrative law judge;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(2)(b): modify the decision of the administrative law judge; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(2)(c): reverse the findings, conclusions, and decision of the administrative law judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-304(3): The Workforce Appeals Board shall promptly notify the parties to any proceedings before it of its decision, including its findings and conclusions, and the decision is a final order of the department unless within 30 days after the date the decision of the Workforce Appeals Board is issued, further appeal is initiated under this title.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-305 Independence of Workforce Appeals Board.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
A member of the Workforce Appeals Board may not participate in any case in which the member is an interested party.  Each decision of a member of the Workforce Appeals Board shall represent the member's independent judgment.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-306 Electronic or similar methods.
--------------------------------------------------------------
The department may by rule permit hearings or other adjudicative hearings to be conducted, recorded, or published by means of electronic devices or other similar methods.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-1-307 Scope of part.
----------------------------------------------
This part does not apply to adjudication under

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-2-204 Job opportunity portal for individuals with criminal histories.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-2-204(1): As used in this section, "web portal" means an Internet webpage that can be accessed by a person who enters the person's unique user information in order to access secure information.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 3 - Employment Support Act
********************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Employment Support Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(1): 63G-4-103 "Adjudicative proceeding" has the same meaning as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(2): "Administrative order" means an order issued by the department that addresses an overpayment of public assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(3): "Applicant" means a person who requests assistance under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(4): 35A-3-118 "Approved self-reliance training" means an educational class, training session, or counseling session:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(4)(a): approved by the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(4)(b): 35A-3-118 described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(4)(c): provided at no cost to a client.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(5): "Assignment of support" means the transfer to the state of a recipient's right to receive support from another person that accrues during the period the recipient receives public assistance, including a right to receive support on behalf of any family member for whom the recipient is applying for or receiving assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(6): "Average monthly number of families" means the average number of families who received cash assistance on a monthly basis during the previous federal fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(7): 35A-3-302 "Cash assistance" means the monthly dollar amount a recipient is eligible to receive under the Family Employment Program under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(8): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act "Child care services" means care of a child by a responsible person who is not the child's parent or legal guardian, for a portion of the day that is less than 24 hours in a qualified setting, as defined by rules made by the department in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(9)(a): "Civic organization" means an organization that provides services to its community.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(9)(b): "Civic organization" includes a community service club or organization, a charitable health care or service organization, a fraternal organization, a labor union, a minority or ethnic organization, a commercial or industrial organization, a commerce or business club, a private nonprofit organization, a private nonprofit corporation that provides funding to a community service organization, an organization that advocates or provides for the needs of persons with low incomes, a religious organization, and an organization that fosters strong neighborhoods and communities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(10): "Core programs" means the following activities as described in 29 U.S.C. Sec.  3102:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(10)(a): youth services;

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(10)(e): employment services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(10)(f): vocational rehabilitation services.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(11): "Court order" means a judgment or order of a court of this state, another state, or the federal government that addresses an overpayment of public assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(12): "Date of enrollment" means the date on which the applicant was approved as eligible for cash assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(13): "Director" means the director of the division assigned by the department to administer a program.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(14): 35A-3-303; Part 3, Family Employment Program "Diversion" or "diversion payment" means a one-time cash assistance payment under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-102(15): "Education or training" means education or training in accordance with 29 U.S.C. Sec. 3174 and includes:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103 Department responsibilities.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(3): cooperate with the federal government in the administration of public assistance programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(4): administer state employment services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(5): provide for the compilation of necessary or desirable information, statistics, and reports;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(6): perform other duties and functions required by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(7): monitor the application of eligibility policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(8): develop personnel training programs for effective and efficient operation of the programs administered by the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(9): 35A-3-701 provide refugee resettlement services in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(10): Part 2, Office of Child Care provide child care assistance for children in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(11): provide services that enable an applicant or recipient to qualify for affordable housing in cooperation with:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(11)(a): the Utah Housing Corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(11)(b): the Housing and Community Development Division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(11)(c): local housing authorities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(12): administer the Medicaid Eligibility Quality Control function in accordance with 42 C.F.R. Sec. 431.812; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103(13): Title 26B, Chapter 3, Health Care - Administration and Assistance; Title 26B, Chapter 3, Part 9, Utah Children's Health Insurance Program conduct non-clinical eligibility hearings and issue final decisions in adjudicative proceedings, including expedited appeals as defined in 42 C.F.R. Sec. 431.224, for medical assistance eligibility under:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5 Employment and the provision of services for the disabled.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(1): As used in this section, "recipient" means an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(1)(a): has a disability;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(1)(b): suffers from a mental illness; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(1)(c): is undergoing treatment for a substance abuse problem.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(2): Subject to funds made available for this purpose and subject to federal and state law, when providing services to a recipient in the programs provided under this chapter, the department shall give priority to providing services that assist an eligible recipient in obtaining and retaining meaningful and gainful employment that enables the recipient to earn sufficient income to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(2)(a): purchase goods and services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(2)(b): establish self-sufficiency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(2)(c): exercise economic control of the recipient's life.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3): (2); (2) The department shall develop a written plan to implement the policy described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(a): assessing the strengths and needs of a recipient;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(b): customizing strength-based approaches to obtaining employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(c): expecting, encouraging, providing, and rewarding employment:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(c)(i): integrated employment in the workplace at competitive wages and benefits; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(c)(ii): self-employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(d): developing partnerships with potential employers;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(e): maximizing appropriate employment training opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(f): coordinating services with other government agencies and community resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(g): (2) to the extent possible, eliminating practices and policies that interfere with the policy described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(3)(h): arranging sub-minimum wage work or volunteer work for an eligible recipient when employment at market rates cannot be obtained.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(4): (2); (3); (3) The department shall, on an annual basis:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-103.5(4)(a): (2); (3) set goals to implement the policy described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-104 Contracts for administration and provision of public assistance.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department may contract with other public or private agencies to assist in the administration and provision of public assistance.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-105 Determination of eligibility and responsibility -- Information from State Tax Commission.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-105(1): The department may have access to relevant information contained in the income tax returns of an applicant, a recipient, or a person who has a duty to support an applicant or recipient, in determining:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-105(1)(a): eligibility for public assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-105(1)(b): payment responsibilities for institutional care; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-105(1)(c): any other administrative purpose consistent with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-105(2): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act The information requested by the department shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-105(2)(a): provided by the State Tax Commission on forms furnished by the department; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-105(2)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act treated by the department as a private record under


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-106 Residency requirements.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-106(1): An applicant is only eligible for public assistance under this chapter if the applicant is living in Utah voluntarily with the intention of making the state the applicant's place of residence.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-106(2): An applicant is not eligible for public assistance under this chapter if the applicant is living in Utah for a temporary purpose.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108 Assignment of support.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(1)(a): An applicant shall provide an assignment of support to the department regardless of whether the payment is court ordered.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(1)(b): (1)(a) Upon the receipt of public assistance, any right of the recipient to receive support from another person passes to the state, including a right to support on behalf of any family member for whom the recipient is applying for or receiving assistance, even if the recipient has not executed and delivered an assignment of support to the department as required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(2): An assignment of support, or a right to receive support passed to the state, includes payments ordered, decreed, or adjudged by a court within this state, another state, or a territory of the United States and is not in lieu of, and does not supersede or alter, any other court order, decree, or judgment.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(3): When an assignment of support is executed or the right to support passes to the state under this section, the recipient is eligible to regular monthly assistance and the support paid to the state is a refund.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(4): All money refunded under this section shall be deposited into the General Fund, except any amount which is required to be credited to the federal government.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(5): On and after the date a recipient stops receiving cash assistance, an assignment of support under this section does not apply to support that accrued before the recipient received the cash assistance if:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(5)(a): the state has not collected the support by the date the recipient stops receiving cash assistance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(5)(b): the assignment was executed on or after October 1, 1998.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(6): The state shall distribute arrearages to a recipient in accordance with the requirements of the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C. Sec. 657.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-108(7): When an assignment of support includes child support, the total amount of child support assigned to the state and collected under this section may not exceed the total amount of cash assistance received by the recipient.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109 Assistance provided to guardian or other caretaker -- Periodic review.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(1): At the discretion of the department, the department may pay the public assistance to the legal guardian of a recipient.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(2): Part 3, Family Employment Program The department may only provide cash assistance on behalf of an eligible recipient under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(2)(a): by reason of the recipient's physical or mental condition, the recipient is unable to manage funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(2)(b): the provision of cash assistance directly to the recipient would be contrary to the recipient's welfare; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(2)(c): the department is acting according to federal requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(3): The department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(3)(a): undertake or contract with other state agencies to make special efforts to protect the welfare of a recipient and improve the recipient's capacity for self-care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(3)(b): periodically review a recipient's condition to determine whether, in the best interest of the recipient:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(3)(b)(i): cash assistance that is provided to an individual other than the recipient should be discontinued; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-109(3)(b)(ii): a legal guardian should be appointed.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-110 Third party obligation -- Interest.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-110(1): If the department expends public assistance on behalf of a recipient for services or supplies, for which another person is obligated to reimburse the department, the department shall notify the person of the obligation to make the reimbursement.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-110(2): (1) Upon receiving notification under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-110(3): (2) After the time period established under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-111 Collection of overpayments.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-111(1): 35A-3-603 The department shall recover overpayments as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-111(2): An excess property lien that is required by a department program, but is not transferred to the federal government, remains a condition of eligibility in public assistance programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-111(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act A recipient may appeal an initial department determination that there has been an overpayment under rules made by the department in accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-112 Assistance not assignable -- Exemption from execution, garnishment, bankruptcy, or insolvency proceedings.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-112(1): Public assistance provided under this chapter is not assignable at law or in equity.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-112(2): None of the money paid or payable under this chapter is subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-112(2)(a): execution, levy, attachment, garnishment, or other legal process; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-112(2)(b): the operation of bankruptcy or insolvency law.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-113 Prohibition of charges or fees for representing applicants or recipients.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Except for criminal proceedings, a person may not charge or receive a fee for representing an applicant or recipient in a proceeding under this chapter, or with respect to an application, in an amount greater than the amount determined by the court or body before whom an applicant or recipient has been represented regardless of who pays the charge or fee.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118 Self-reliance training.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(1): If the department determines that it is not prohibited under federal law or regulation, a client who is at least 21 years old, but who is younger than 65 years old, and who is receiving public assistance under this chapter, shall complete at least two hours of approved self-reliance training within 90 days of the first day of receiving public assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(2): If the department determines that federal law or regulation regarding a specific service or benefit under this chapter prohibits requiring a client to complete at least two hours of self-reliance training within 90 days of first receiving public assistance, the department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(2)(a): seek a waiver from the appropriate federal agency to allow requiring the training; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(2)(b): inform the client about the option of completing self-reliance training.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3): The department shall ensure that approved self-reliance training:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(a): is designed to help clients learn to become financially stable and less dependent on government assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(b): teaches skills and knowledge that will assist clients in becoming self-reliant;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(c): is available at sufficient times and places to enable clients to reasonably complete the training;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(d): is offered at no cost to clients;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(e): includes an option for online training; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(f): is provided and taught in a manner that is sensitive to the specific needs and challenges of clients, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(f)(i): employment situations and work schedules;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(f)(ii): health or disability related employment issues;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(f)(iii): family care responsibilities and schedules; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(3)(f)(iv): transportation issues.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(4): 35A-3-102 Approved self-reliance training may be offered by the department or any of the following if approved by the department:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(4)(a): 35A-3-102 a civic organization as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(4)(b): a for-profit entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(4)(c): an educational institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(4)(d): any state or local entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(5): 35A-3-507 The director may contract with a civic organization to provide approved self-reliance training, if the director follows the procedures for contracting with a civic organization for the provision of social capital as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(6): 35A-1-109; (2)(a) As part of the annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(6)(a): describe what entities are providing approved self-reliance training;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(6)(b): provide the number of clients who have completed at least two hours of approved self-reliance training;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(6)(c): describe any services or benefits under this chapter that may not be conditioned on the completion of self-reliance training because of federal law or regulation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(6)(d): (2)(a) describe the response to any waiver request described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-118(7): (1) A client's completion of the approved self-reliance training described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(1): 35A-3-102 "Child care" means the child care services defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(1)(a): children age 12 or younger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(1)(b): children with disabilities age 18 or younger.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(2): "Child care provider association" means an association:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(2)(a): that has functioned as a child care provider association in the state for at least three years; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(2)(b): is affiliated with a national child care provider association.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(3): 35A-3-205 "Committee" means the Child Care Advisory Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(4): "Director" means the director of the Office of Child Care.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5): 35A-3-203
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(a): 35A-3-203 "Income" means gross income, whether earned or unearned, as defined by rule made in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b): "Income" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b)(i): income from means-tested programs, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b)(i)(A): Temporary Assistance to Needy Families;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b)(i)(B): the Social Security Act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b)(i)(C): the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b)(ii): in-kind income;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b)(iii): scholarship, grant, or bona fide loan money;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b)(iv): a federal or state income tax credit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(5)(b)(v): a nonrecurring lump sum benefit.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(6): 35A-3-203 "Income-eligible child" means a child whose:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(6)(a): family income does not exceed 85% of state median income for a family of the same size; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(6)(b): 35A-3-203 family assets do not exceed the limit established by the office through rule created in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-201(7): 35A-3-202 "Office" means the Office of Child Care created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-202 Creation.
-----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-202(1): There is created within the Department of Workforce Services an Office of Child Care.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-202(2): The office shall be administered by a director who shall be appointed by the executive director and who may be removed from that position at the will of the executive director.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203 Functions and duties of office -- Annual report.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The office shall:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(1): assess critical child care needs throughout the state on an ongoing basis and focus its activities on helping to meet the most critical needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(2): provide child care subsidy services for income-eligible children through age 12 and for income-eligible children with disabilities through age 18;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(3): provide information:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(3)(a): to employers for the development of options for child care in the work place; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(3)(b): for educating the public in obtaining quality child care;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(4): coordinate services for quality:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(4)(a): child care training;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(4)(b): child care resource and referral core services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(4)(c): training and education regarding child behavioral health interventions and competencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(5): apply for, accept, or expend gifts or donations from public or private sources;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(6): provide administrative support services to the committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(7): work collaboratively with the following for the delivery of quality child care, early childhood programs, and school age programs throughout the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(7)(a): the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(7)(b): the Department of Health; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(7)(c): the Division of Substance Abuse and Mental Health within the Department of Human Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(8): research child care programs and public policy to improve the quality and accessibility of child care, early childhood programs, and school age programs in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(9): provide planning and technical assistance for the development and implementation of programs in communities that lack child care, early childhood programs, and school age programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(10): 35A-3-205 provide organizational support for the establishment of nonprofit organizations approved by the Child Care Advisory Committee, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(11): 35A-1-109 coordinate with the department to include in the annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(12): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act make rules, in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(12)(a): establishing the eligibility requirements for a child care provider to receive a grant or subsidy, including for the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(12)(a)(i): providing child care for an income-eligible child who is 12 years old or younger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(12)(a)(ii): providing child care for an income-eligible child with disabilities who is 18 years old or younger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-203(12)(b): prioritizing awards of child care grants or subsidies for income-eligible children within available funds.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-204 Duties of director.
---------------------------------------------------
The director shall:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-204(1): enforce rules made by the department regulating the use of services provided by the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-204(2): supervise office staff and prepare an annual work plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-204(3): apply for, accept, and expend donations from public or private sources to assist the office in fulfilling its statutory obligations.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205 Creation of committee.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(1): There is created a Child Care Advisory Committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(2): The committee shall counsel and advise the office in fulfilling its statutory obligations, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(2)(a): reviewing and providing recommendations on the office's annual budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(2)(b): providing recommendations on how the office might best respond to child care needs throughout the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(2)(c): providing recommendations on the use of money that is provided to the office for the purpose of addressing child care needs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3): The committee is composed of the following members, with special attention given to insure diversity and representation from both urban and rural groups:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(a): one expert in early childhood development;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(b): one child care provider who operates a center;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(c): one child care provider who operates a family child care business;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(d): one parent who is representative of households receiving a child care subsidy from the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(e): one representative from the public at-large;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(f): one representative selected by the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(g): one representative of the Department of Health;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(h): one representative of the Department of Human Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(i): two representatives from the corporate community, one who is a recent "Family Friendly" award winner and who received the award because of efforts related to child care;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(j): two representatives from the small business community;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(k): one representative from child care advocacy groups;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(l): one representative of children with disabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(m): one representative from the state Head Start Association appointed by the association;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(n): one representative from each child care provider association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(3)(o): one representative of a child care resource and referral center appointed by the organization representing child care resource and referral agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(4): (3)(a); (e); (j); (n); (3)(f); (i); (3)(o)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(4)(a): (3)(a); (e); (j); (n) The executive director shall appoint the members designated in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(4)(b): (3)(f); (i) The head of the respective departments shall appoint the members referred to in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(4)(c): (3)(o) Each child care provider association shall appoint its respective member referred to in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(5): (5)(b); (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(5)(a): (5)(b) Except as required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(5)(b): (5)(a) Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(6): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, including missing three consecutive meetings where the member has not been excused by the chair prior to or during the meeting, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(7): A majority of the members constitutes a quorum for the transaction of business.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(8)(a): The executive director shall select a chair from the committee membership.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-205(8)(b): A chair may serve no more than two one-year terms as chair.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209 Award of child care subsidy services.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(1)(a): On or before June 30, 2023, the office shall award a full child care subsidy or grant for an income-eligible child.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(1)(b): (1)(a) The office shall make the award described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(1)(b)(i): in accordance with applicable federal law and regulation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(1)(b)(ii): subject to available funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(2): Beginning on July 1, 2023, the office may award:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(2)(a): a full child care subsidy or grant for an income-eligible child whose family income is equal to or below 75% of state median income; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(2)(b): a progressively lower child care subsidy or grant for each tenth of a percentage point by which the income-eligible child's family income exceeds 75% of state median income up to 85% of state median income.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-209(3): (3)(b); (3)(a); (3)(d); (3)(c)

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-301 Purpose -- Legislative findings.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-301(1): The Legislature finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-301(1)(a): employment improves the quality of life for parents, children, and individuals by increasing family income, developing job skills, and improving self-esteem; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-301(1)(b): the purpose of the cash assistance provided under this part is to assist a parent recipient to obtain employment that is sufficient to sustain a family, to ensure the dignity of those receiving assistance, to prevent families with children from becoming homeless, and to strengthen families.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-301(2): The Legislature recognizes that even with assistance, some recipients may be unable to attain complete self-sufficiency.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302 Eligibility requirements.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(1): There is created the "Family Employment Program" to provide cash assistance under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(2)(a): The department shall submit a state plan to the Secretary of the United States Department of Health and Human Services to obtain funding under the federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families Block Grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(2)(b): The department shall make the state plan consistent with this part and federal law.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(2)(c): If a discrepancy exists between a provision of the state plan and this part, this part supersedes the provision in the state plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(3): The services provided under this part are for both one-parent and two-parent families.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(4): To be eligible for cash assistance under this part, a family shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(4)(a): have at least one minor dependent child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-302(4)(b): have a parent who is in the third trimester of a pregnancy.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303 Diversion.
------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(a): When an applicant applies for cash assistance under this part, the department shall assess whether the applicant should be helped by:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(a)(i): diversion to avoid extended cash assistance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(a)(ii): normal cash assistance under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(b): In completing the assessment under this section, the department may consider the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(b)(i): the applicant's employment history;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(b)(ii): the likelihood of the applicant obtaining immediate full-time employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(b)(iii): the applicant's general prospect for obtaining full-time employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(b)(iv): the applicant's need for cash assistance to pay for housing or substantial and unforeseen expenses or work-related expenses;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(b)(v): housing stability; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(1)(b)(vi): the adequacy of the applicant's child care arrangements, if applicable.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(2): If the department determines that the applicant should be helped by diversion and the applicant agrees with this determination, the department shall provide a single payment of cash assistance up to three times the maximum monthly amount of cash assistance that the applicant would be otherwise qualified to receive based on household size.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-303(3): If the department determines that diversion is not appropriate, an applicant may receive cash assistance as provided in this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304 Assessment -- Participation requirements and limitations -- Employment plan -- Mentors.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(1): (1)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(1)(a): Within 30 business days of the date of enrollment, the department shall provide that a parent recipient:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(1)(a)(i): is assigned an employment counselor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(1)(a)(ii): completes an assessment provided by the department regarding the parent recipient's:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(1)(a)(ii)(A): prior work experience;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(1)(a)(ii)(B): ability to become employable; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(1)(a)(ii)(C): skills.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(1)(b): (1)(a)(ii) The assessment provided under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2): 35A-3-304.5; 35A-3-304.5
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(a): Within 15 business days of a parent recipient completing an assessment:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(a)(i): the department and the parent recipient shall enter into an employment plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(a)(ii): the parent recipient shall complete a written questionnaire, provided by the department, designed to accurately determine the likelihood of the parent recipient having a substance use disorder involving the misuse of a controlled substance.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(b): The employment plan shall have a target date for entry into employment.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(c): The department shall provide a copy of the employment plan to the parent recipient.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(d): For the parent recipient, the employment plan may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(d)(i): job searching requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(d)(ii): if the parent recipient does not have a high school diploma, participation in an educational program to obtain a high school diploma, or its equivalent;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(d)(iii): education or training necessary to obtain employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(d)(iv): a combination of work and education or training; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(d)(v): assisting the Office of Recovery Services in good faith to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(d)(v)(A): establish the paternity of a minor child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(d)(v)(B): establish or enforce a child support order.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(e): 35A-3-304.5; 35A-3-304.5 If the parent recipient tests positive for the unlawful use of a controlled substance after taking a drug test under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-304(2)(e)(i): participate in treatment for a substance use disorder; and

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-309 Information regarding home ownership.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-309(1): The department shall provide information and service coordination to assist an applicant in obtaining affordable housing.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-309(2): The information and services may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-309(2)(a): information from the Utah Housing Corporation and the Housing and Community Development Division regarding special housing programs, including programs for first-time home buyers and individuals with low and moderate incomes and the eligibility requirements for those programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-309(2)(b): referrals to programs operated by volunteers from the real estate industry that assist applicants in obtaining affordable housing, including information on home ownership, down payments, closing costs, and credit requirements; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-309(2)(c): referrals to housing programs operated by municipalities, counties, local housing authorities, and nonprofit housing organizations that assist individuals in obtaining affordable housing, including first-time home ownership.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-311(2)(c)(i): receive available treatment for the dependency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-311(2)(c)(ii): make progress toward overcoming the dependency.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-311(2)(d): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The department may only refer a recipient who is a drug dependent person to a treatment provider for treating drug dependency if the provider has achieved an objective level of success, as defined by department rules made in accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312 Individual development accounts.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(1)(a): "Individual development account" means a trust account funded through periodic contributions by a recipient and matched by or through a not-for-profit organization organized under Section 501(c)(3), Internal Revenue Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(1)(b): "Qualified acquisition costs" means the costs of acquiring, constructing, or reconstructing a residence, including settlement and closing costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(1)(c): "Qualified businesses capitalization expenses" means expenditures for capital, plant, equipment, working capital, and inventory.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(2): An individual development account may be established by or on behalf of a recipient to enable the recipient to accumulate funds for the following purposes:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(2)(a): postsecondary educational expenses, including tuition, fees, books, supplies, and transportation costs, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(2)(a)(i): the recipient has terminated cash assistance under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(2)(a)(ii): the expenses are paid from the individual development account directly to an educational institution that the recipient is attending as part of an employment plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(2)(b): qualified acquisition costs associated with a first-time home purchase if paid from the individual development account directly to a person to whom the amount is due;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(2)(c): amounts paid from an individual development account directly to a business capitalization account that is established in a federally insured financial institution and used solely for qualified business capitalization expenses; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(2)(d): the purchase of assistive technologies, vehicle modifications, or home improvements to allow a recipient with a disability to participate in work-related activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-3-312(3): A recipient may only deposit earned income and funds received from a not-for-profit organization into an individual development account.
