Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-403.5(2)(c): the federal government has agreed to reimburse the department for the cost of paying the benefit for that week.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-404 Eligibility for benefits after receiving workers' compensation or occupational disease compensation.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-404(1): Notwithstanding any requirements involving base periods or other benefit compensational factors provided for under this chapter a person who has had a continuous period of sickness or injury for which the person was compensated under the workers' compensation or the occupational disease laws of this state or under federal law shall, if the person is otherwise eligible, thereafter be entitled to receive the unemployment compensation benefits the person would have been entitled to receive under the law and regulations based on the person's potential eligibility at the time of the person's last employment.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-404(2): Benefit rights are not preserved under this section unless the individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-404(2)(a): files a claim for benefits with respect to a week no later than 90 days after the end of the continuous period of sickness or injury; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-404(2)(b): files the claim with respect to a week within the 36-month period immediately following the commencement of such period of sickness or injury.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405 Ineligibility for benefits.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in SubsectionUtah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1): (1)(e); (1); (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(a): For the week in which the claimant left work voluntarily without good cause, if so found by the division, and for each week thereafter until the claimant has performed services in bona fide, covered employment and earned wages for those services equal to at least six times the claimant's weekly benefit amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(b): A claimant may not be denied eligibility for benefits if the claimant leaves work under circumstances where it would be contrary to equity and good conscience to impose a disqualification.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(c): Using available information from employers and the claimant, the division shall consider for the purposes of this chapter the reasonableness of the claimant's actions, and the extent to which the actions evidence a genuine continuing attachment to the labor market in reaching a determination of whether the ineligibility of a claimant is contrary to equity and good conscience.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(d): (1)(e); (1) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(e): (1) A claimant who has left work voluntarily to accompany or follow the claimant's spouse to a new locality does so with good cause for purposes of this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(e)(i): the claimant's spouse is a member of the United States armed forces and the claimant's spouse has been relocated by a full-time assignment scheduled to last at least 180 days while on:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(e)(i)(A): active duty as defined in 10 U.S.C. Sec. 101(d)(1); or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(e)(i)(B): active guard or reserve duty as defined in 10 U.S.C. Sec. 101(d)(6);
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(e)(ii): it is impractical as determined by the division for the claimant to commute to the previous work from the new locality;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(e)(iii): the claimant left work voluntarily no earlier than 15 days before the scheduled start date of the spouse's active-duty assignment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(1)(e)(iv): the claimant otherwise meets and follows the eligibility and reporting requirements of this chapter, including registering for work with the division or, if the claimant has relocated to another state, the equivalent agency of that state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(2)(a): For the week in which the claimant was discharged for just cause or for an act or omission in connection with employment, not constituting a crime, which is deliberate, willful, or wanton and adverse to the employer's rightful interest, if so found by the division, and thereafter until the claimant has earned an amount equal to at least six times the claimant's weekly benefit amount in bona fide covered employment.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(2)(b): For the week in which the claimant was discharged for dishonesty constituting a crime or any felony or class A misdemeanor in connection with the claimant's work as shown by the facts, together with the claimant's admission, or as shown by the claimant's conviction of that crime in a court of competent jurisdiction and for the 51 next following weeks.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(2)(c): Wage credits shall be deleted from the claimant's base period, and are not available for this or any subsequent claim for benefits.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(a)(i): If the division finds that the claimant has failed without good cause to properly apply for available suitable work, to accept a referral to suitable work offered by the employment office, or to accept suitable work offered by an employer or the employment office.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(a)(ii): The ineligibility continues until the claimant has performed services in bona fide covered employment and earned wages for the services in an amount equal to at least six times the claimant's weekly benefit amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(b)(i): A claimant may not be denied eligibility for benefits for failure to apply, accept referral, or accept available suitable work under circumstances where it would be contrary to equity and good conscience to impose a disqualification.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(b)(ii): The division shall consider the purposes of this chapter, the reasonableness of the claimant's actions, and the extent to which the actions evidence a genuine continuing attachment to the labor market in reaching a determination of whether the ineligibility of a claimant is contrary to equity and good conscience.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(c): In determining whether work is suitable for an individual, the division shall consider the:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(c)(i): degree of risk involved to the individual's health, safety, and morals;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(c)(ii): individual's physical fitness and prior training;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(c)(iii): individual's prior earnings and experience;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(c)(iv): individual's length of unemployment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(c)(v): prospects for securing local work in the individual's customary occupation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(c)(vi): wages for similar work in the locality; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(c)(vii): distance of the available work from the individual's residence.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(d): Prior earnings shall be considered on the basis of all four quarters used in establishing eligibility and not just the earnings from the most recent employer.  The division shall be more prone to find work as suitable the longer the claimant has been unemployed and the less likely the prospects are to secure local work in his customary occupation.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(e): Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, no work is suitable, and benefits may not be denied under this chapter to any otherwise eligible individual for refusing to accept new work under any of the following conditions:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(e)(i): if the position offered is vacant due directly to a strike, lockout, or other labor dispute;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(e)(ii): if the wages, hours, or other conditions of the work offered are substantially less favorable to the individual than those prevailing for similar work in the locality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(3)(e)(iii): if as a condition of being employed the individual would be required to join a company union or to resign from or refrain from joining any bona fide labor organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(4): (4); 35A-4-401(4); 35A-4-403(1)(f) For any week in which the division finds that the claimant's unemployment is due to a stoppage of work that exists because of a strike involving the claimant's grade, class, or group of workers at the factory or establishment at which the claimant is or was last employed.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(4)(a): If the division finds that a strike has been fomented by a worker of any employer, none of the workers of the grade, class, or group of workers of the individual who is found to be a party to the plan, or agreement to foment a strike, shall be eligible for benefits.  However, if the division finds that the strike is caused by the failure or refusal of any employer to conform to any law of the state or of the United States pertaining to hours, wages, or other conditions of work, the strike may not render the workers ineligible for benefits.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-405(4)(b): If the division finds that the employer, the employer's agent or representative has conspired, planned, or agreed with any of the employer's workers, their agents or representatives to foment a strike, that strike may not render the workers ineligible for benefits.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406 Claims for benefits -- Continuing jurisdiction -- Appeal -- Notice of decision -- Repayment of benefits fraudulently received.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(1)(a): Claims for benefits shall be made and shall be determined by the division or referred to an administrative law judge in accordance with rules adopted by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(1)(b): Each employer shall post and maintain in places readily accessible to individuals in his service printed statements concerning benefit rights, claims for benefits, and the other matters relating to the administration of this chapter as prescribed by rule of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(1)(c): Each employer shall supply to individuals in his service copies of the printed statements or other materials relating to claims for benefits when and as the department may by rule prescribe.  The printed statements and other materials shall be supplied by the division to each employer without cost to the employer.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(2): (4)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(2)(a): Jurisdiction over benefits shall be continuous.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(2)(b): Upon its own initiative or upon application of any party affected, the division may on the basis of change in conditions or because of a mistake as to facts, review a decision allowing or disallowing in whole or in part a claim for benefits.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(2)(c): The review shall be conducted in accordance with rules adopted by the department and may result in a new decision that may award, terminate, continue, increase, or decrease benefits, or may result in a referral of the claim to an appeal tribunal.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(2)(d): Notice of any redetermination shall be promptly given to the party applying for redetermination and to other parties entitled to notice of the original determination, in the manner prescribed in this section with respect to notice of an original determination.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(2)(e): The new order shall be subject to review and appeal as provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(2)(f): (4) A review may not be made after one year from the date of the original determination, except in cases of fraud or claimant fault as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(3): 35A-4-508; Chapter 1, Part 3, Adjudicative Proceedings
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(3)(a): The claimant or any other party entitled to notice of a determination as provided by department rule may file an appeal from the determination with the Division of Adjudication within 10 days after the date of mailing of the notice of determination or redetermination to the party's last-known address or, if the notice is not mailed, within 10 days after the date of delivery of the notice.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(3)(b): Unless the appeal or referral is withdrawn with  permission of the administrative law judge, after affording the parties reasonable opportunity for a fair hearing, the administrative law judge shall make findings and conclusions and on that basis affirm, modify, or reverse the determination or redetermination.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(3)(c): The administrative law judge shall first give notice of the pendency of an appeal to the  division, which may then be a party to the proceedings.  The administrative law judge shall receive into the record of the appeal any documents or other records provided by the division, and may obtain or request any additional documents or records held by the division or any of the parties that the administrative law judge considers relevant to the proper determination of the appeal.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(3)(d): The parties shall be promptly notified of the administrative law judge's decision and shall be furnished with a copy of the decision and the findings and conclusions in support of the decision.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(3)(e): 35A-4-508; Chapter 1, Part 3, Adjudicative Proceedings The decision is considered to be final unless, within 30 days after the date of mailing of notice and a copy of the decision to the party's last-known address, or in the absence of mailed notice, within 30 days after the delivery of the notice, further appeal is initiated in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(4)(a): Any person who, by reason of his fraud, has received any sum as benefits under this chapter to which he was not entitled shall repay the sum to the division for the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(4)(b): If any person, by reason of his own fault, has received any sum as benefits under this chapter to which under a redetermination or decision pursuant to this section he has been found not entitled, he shall repay the sum, or shall, in the discretion of the division, have the sum deducted from any future benefits payable to him, or both.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(4)(c): In any case in which under this subsection a claimant is liable to repay to the division any sum for the fund, the sum shall be collectible in the same manner as provided for contributions due under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(5)(a): If any person has received any sum as benefits under this chapter to which under a redetermination or decision he was not entitled, and it has been found that he was without fault in the matter, he is not liable to repay the sum but shall be liable to have the sum deducted from any future benefits payable to him.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-406(5)(b): The division may waive recovery of the overpayment if it is shown to the satisfaction of the division that the claimant has the inability to meet more than the basic needs of survival for an indefinite period lasting at least several months.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407 Voluntary income tax withholding.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(1): The department shall advise an individual filing a new claim for benefits at the time of filing the claim that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(1)(a): unemployment benefits may be subject to federal, state, and local income tax;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(1)(b): there are requirements for estimating tax payments;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(1)(c): the individual may elect to have federal income tax deducted and withheld from the individual's payment of benefits at the amount specified by the Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(1)(d): the individual may elect to have state income tax deducted and withheld from the individual's payment of benefits at the rate of 5%; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(1)(e): the individual may change a previously elected withholding status.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(2): (1) Amounts deducted and withheld from benefits for income taxes under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(3)(a): The department shall follow all procedures specified by the United States Department of Labor, the Internal Revenue Service, and the State Tax Commission pertaining to deducting, withholding, and submitting amounts deducted and withheld for income taxes.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(3)(b): Amounts deducted and withheld for income taxes under this section shall be deducted and withheld only after amounts are deducted and withheld for:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(3)(b)(i): overpayment of unemployment compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(3)(b)(ii): child support obligations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-407(3)(b)(iii): any other amount required to be deducted and withheld under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501 Unemployment Compensation Fund -- Administration -- Contents -- Treasurer and custodian -- Separate accounts -- Use of money requisitioned -- Advances under Social Security Act.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1): 35A-4-306(5)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1)(a): There is established the Unemployment Compensation Fund, separate and apart from all public money or funds of this state, that shall be administered by the department exclusively for the purposes of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1)(b): 35A-4-306(5) This fund shall consist of the following money, all of which shall be mingled and undivided:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1)(b)(i): 35A-4-306(5) all contributions collected under this chapter, less refunds of contributions made from the clearing account under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1)(b)(ii): interest earned upon any money in the fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1)(b)(iii): any property or securities acquired through the use of money belonging to the fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1)(b)(iv): all earnings of the property or securities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1)(b)(v): all money credited to this state's account in the unemployment trust fund under Section 903 of the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C. 1101 et seq., as amended; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(1)(b)(vi): all other money received for the fund from any other source.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2): 35A-4-205(1)(a); 35A-4-306(5)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(a): The state treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(a)(i): be the treasurer and custodian of the fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(a)(ii): administer the fund in accordance with the directions of the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(a)(iii): pay all warrants drawn upon it by the division or its duly authorized agent in accordance with rules made by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(b): The division shall maintain within the fund three separate accounts:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(b)(i): a clearing account;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(b)(ii): an unemployment trust fund account; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(b)(iii): a benefit account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(c): All money payable to the fund, upon receipt by the division, shall be immediately deposited in the clearing account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(d): 35A-4-205(1)(a); 35A-4-306(5)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(d)(i): All money in the clearing account after clearance shall, except as otherwise provided in this section, be deposited immediately with the secretary of the treasury of the United States of America to the credit of the account of this state in the unemployment trust fund, established and maintained under Section 904 of the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C. 1104, as amended, any provisions of law in this state relating to the deposit, administration, release, or disbursement of money in the possession or custody of this state to the contrary notwithstanding.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(d)(ii): 35A-4-205(1)(a); 35A-4-306(5) Refunds of contributions payable under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(e): The benefit account shall consist of all money requisitioned from this state's account in the unemployment trust fund in the United States treasury.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(f): Money in the clearing and benefit accounts may be deposited in any depository bank in which general funds of this state may be deposited, but no public deposit insurance charge or premium may be paid out of the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(g): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(g)(i): Money in the clearing and benefit accounts may not be commingled with other state funds, but shall be maintained in separate accounts on the books of the depository bank.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(g)(ii): The money shall be secured by the depository bank to the same extent and in the same manner as required by the general depository law of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(g)(iii): Collateral pledged for this purpose shall be kept separate and distinct from any collateral pledged to secure other funds of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(h): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(h)(i): The state treasurer is liable on the state treasurer's official bond for the faithful performance of the state treasurer's duties in connection with the unemployment compensation fund provided for under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(h)(ii): The liability on the official bond shall be effective immediately upon the enactment of this provision, and that liability shall exist in addition to the liability upon any separate bond existent on the effective date of this provision, or which may be given in the future.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(2)(h)(iii): All sums recovered for losses sustained by the fund shall be deposited in the fund.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(3)(c): (2) Any balance of money requisitioned from the unemployment trust fund that remains unclaimed or unpaid in the benefit account after the expiration of the period for which the sums were requisitioned shall either be deducted from estimates for, and may be utilized for the payment of, benefits and refunds during succeeding periods, or in the discretion of the division, shall be redeposited with the secretary of the treasury of the United States of America to the credit of the state's account in the unemployment trust fund, as provided in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(4)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(4)(b)(i): When the unemployment trust fund ceases to exist, or the separate book account is no longer maintained, all money belonging to the unemployment compensation fund of the state shall be administered by the division as a trust fund for the purpose of paying benefits under this chapter, and the division shall have authority to hold, invest, transfer, sell, deposit, and release the money, and any properties, securities, or earnings acquired as an incident to the administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(4)(b)(ii): The money shall be invested in readily marketable bonds or other interest-bearing obligations of the United States of America, of the state, or of any county, city, town, or school district of the state, at current market prices for the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-501(4)(b)(iii): The investment shall be made so that all the assets of the fund shall always be readily convertible into cash when needed for the payment of benefits.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-503 Destruction or disposal of records or reports by division -- Procedure.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The division may destroy or dispose of reports or records that are properly recorded or summarized in the payment records of the division, or that are no longer necessary in the proper administration of this chapter in accordance with an applicable records retention schedule approved by the Records Management Committee under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-506 Special Administrative Expense Account.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508 Review of decision or determination by division -- Administrative law judge -- Division of adjudication -- Workforce Appeals Board -- Judicial review by Court of Appeals -- Exclusive procedure.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(1)(a): A review of a decision or determination involving contribution liability or applications for refund of contributions shall be made by the division in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(1)(b): The division in conducting the review may in its discretion:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(1)(b)(i): refer the matter to an administrative law judge;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(1)(b)(ii): decide the application for review on the basis of any facts and information as may be obtained; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(1)(b)(iii): hear argument or hold an informal hearing to secure further facts.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(1)(c): After the review, notice of the decision shall be given to the employing unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(1)(d): The decision made pursuant to the review is the final decision of the division unless, within 10 days after the date of notification or mailing of the decision, a further appeal is initiated under the provisions of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(2): (1); Chapter 1, Part 3, Adjudicative Proceedings
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(2)(a): (1) Within 10 days after the mailing or personal delivery of a notice of a determination or decision rendered following a review under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(2)(b): The administrative law judge shall give notice of the pendency of the appeal to the division and any parties entitled to notice as provided by department rule.  The administrative law judge shall receive into the record of the appeal any documents or other records provided by the division, and may obtain or request any additional documents or records held by the division or any of the parties that the administrative law judge considers relevant to a proper determination of the appeal.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(2)(c): After affording the parties reasonable opportunity for a fair hearing, the administrative law judge shall make findings and conclusions and on that basis affirm, modify, or reverse the determination of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(2)(d): The parties and the division shall be promptly notified of the administrative law judge's decision and furnished a copy of the decision and findings.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(2)(e): Chapter 1, Part 3, Adjudicative Proceedings The decision of the administrative law judge is considered to be a final order of the department unless within 30 days after the date the decision of the administrative law judge is issued further appeal is initiated under this section and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(3): 35A-4-502(4)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(3)(a): 35A-4-502(4)(a) The director of the Division of Adjudication shall assign an impartial, salaried administrative law judge selected in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(3)(b): All records on appeals shall be maintained in the offices of the Division of Adjudication.  The records shall include an appeal docket showing the receipt and disposition of the appeals on review.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(4): The Workforce Appeals Board may review and decide an appeal from a decision of an administrative law judge issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(5)(a): The manner in which disputed matters are presented, the reports required from the claimant and employing units, and the conduct of hearings and appeals shall be in accordance with rules prescribed by the department for determining the rights of the parties, whether or not the rules conform to common-law or statutory rules of evidence and other technical rules of procedure.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(5)(b): When the same or substantially similar evidence is relevant and material to the matters in issue in more than one proceeding, the same time and place for considering each matter may be fixed, hearings jointly conducted, a single record of the proceedings made, and evidence introduced with respect to one proceeding considered as introduced in the others, if in the judgment of the administrative law judge having jurisdiction of the proceedings, the consolidation would not be prejudicial to any party.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(6): 35A-4-406(2)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(6)(a): 35A-4-406(2) Except for reconsideration of any determination under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(6)(b): Any findings of fact or law, judgment, conclusion, or final order made by an unemployment insurance hearing officer, administrative law judge, or any person with the authority to make findings of fact or law in any action or proceeding before the unemployment insurance appeals tribunal, is not conclusive or binding in any separate or subsequent action or proceeding, between an individual and the individual's present or prior employer, brought before an arbitrator, court, or judge of this state or the United States, regardless of whether the prior action was between the same or related parties or involved the same facts.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(7)(a): Any decision in the absence of an appeal as provided becomes final upon issuance and judicial review may be permitted only after any party claiming to be aggrieved has exhausted the party's remedies before the department as provided by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(7)(b): The division is a party to any judicial action involving any decisions and shall be represented in the judicial action by any qualified attorney employed by the department and designated by it for that purpose or at the division's request by the attorney general.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(8)(a): Within 30 days after the decision of the Workforce Appeals Board is issued, any aggrieved party may secure judicial review by commencing an action in the court of appeals against the Workforce Appeals Board for the review of its decision, in which action any other party to the proceeding before the Workforce Appeals Board shall be made a defendant.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(8)(b): In that action a petition, that shall state the grounds upon which a review is sought, shall be served upon the Workforce Appeals Board or upon that person the Workforce Appeals Board designates.  This service is considered completed service on all parties but there shall be left with the party served as many copies of the petition as there are defendants and the Workforce Appeals Board shall mail one copy to each defendant.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(8)(c): With its answer, the Workforce Appeals Board shall certify and file with the court all documents and papers and a transcript of all testimony taken in the matter together with its findings of fact and decision, in accordance with the requirements of the Utah Rules of Appellate Procedure.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(8)(d): The Workforce Appeals Board may certify to the court questions of law involved in any decision by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(8)(e): In any judicial proceeding under this section, the findings of the Workforce Appeals Board as to the facts, if supported by evidence, are conclusive and the jurisdiction of the court is confined to questions of law.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(8)(f): It is not necessary in any judicial proceeding under this section to enter exceptions to the rulings of the division, an administrative law judge, Workforce Appeals Board and no bond is required for entering the appeal.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(8)(g): Upon final determination of the judicial proceeding, the division shall enter an order in accordance with the determination.  In no event may a petition for judicial review act as a supersedeas.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-4-508(9): The procedure provided for hearings and decisions with respect to any decision or determination of the division affecting claimants or employing units under this chapter is the sole and exclusive procedure notwithstanding any other provision of this title.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-301 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Tax Credit for Employment of Persons Who Are Homeless Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(1): "Date of hire" means the date a person who is homeless first performs labor or services for compensation for an employer.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(2): 59-2-511 "Governmental entity" is as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(3): "Permanent housing, permanent supportive, or transitional facility" means a facility:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(3)(a): located within the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(3)(b): that provides supervision of residents of the facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(3)(c): that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(3)(c)(i): a publicly or privately operated shelter:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(3)(c)(i)(A): designed to provide temporary living accommodations, including a welfare hotel, congregate shelter, or transitional housing for the mentally ill; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(3)(c)(i)(B): that receives federal homeless assistance funding distributed by the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(3)(c)(ii): an emergency shelter that receives homeless assistance funding from a county, city, or town.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(4): "Person who is homeless" means an individual whose primary nighttime residence is:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(4)(a): a public or private place not designated for or ordinarily used as a regular sleeping accommodation for an individual, including a car, park, abandoned building, bus station, train station, airport, or camping ground; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(4)(b): a publicly or privately operated shelter designated to provide temporary living arrangements, including a permanent housing, permanent supportive, or transitional facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(5): "Wage requirement" means that an employer pays a person who is homeless $4,000 or more in wages during a time period that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(5)(a): begins on the date of hire; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-302(5)(b): ends no later than two calendar quarters after the calendar quarter in which the date of hire occurs.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303 Application for tax credit certificate.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(1): An employer who employs a person who is homeless and seeks to receive a tax credit certificate under this part shall file an application with the department with respect to each person who is homeless that the employer employs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(2): The application shall be on a form the department provides to the employer.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3): The application shall require the employer to certify that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3)(a): the person who the employer employs:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3)(a)(i): met the definition of a person who is homeless on the date of hire or at any time during the 60-day period immediately before the date of hire;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3)(a)(ii): is an employee, and not an independent contractor, of the employer;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3)(a)(iii): is legally eligible to work in the United States; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3)(a)(iv): has not worked for the employer for more than 40 hours during the 60-day period immediately before the date of hire; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3)(b): the employer:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3)(b)(i): complies with all state, federal, or local requirements related to the employment of the person who is homeless; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(3)(b)(ii): is not a governmental entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(4): The application:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(4)(a): shall list, for each person who is homeless that the employer employs:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(4)(a)(i): the person's name;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(4)(a)(ii): the person's social security number; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(4)(a)(iii): the person's current address;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(4)(b): shall list the employer's federal employer identification number; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(4)(c): may require additional information as determined by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(5): An employer shall provide documentation to the department to support the certifications and other information the employer provides in the application described in this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-5-303(7): (3); (4) If the department determines that, on the basis of the documentation and other information the employer provides, the employer has not satisfied the certification requirements of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 6 - Apprenticeship Act
****************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter shall be known as the "Apprenticeship Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter and inUtah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(1): "Apprentice" means an individual who has entered into:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(1)(a): a written agreement approved by the Office of Apprenticeship with an employer or the employer's agent, an association of employers, an organization of employees, or a joint committee representing employers and employees;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(1)(b): an apprenticeship that meets Office of Apprenticeship standards; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(1)(c): an apprenticeship that can be completed at no charge to the participant where the participant learns and works with registered standards to learn a set of skills that result in the participant qualifying for a state license or certification or earning industry recognized credentials at the completion of the apprenticeship.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(2): "Apprenticeship" means an industry-driven, high-quality career pathway where employers can develop and prepare their future workforce, and individuals can obtain paid work experience, classroom instruction, and a portable, nationally recognized credential.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(3): 35A-6-105 "Commissioner" means the Commissioner of Apprenticeship Programs described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(4): "Office of Apprenticeship" means the federal agency designated by the United States Department of Labor to oversee apprenticeship programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(5): "Pre-apprenticeship" means a program or set of strategies that is designed to prepare individuals to enter and succeed in an apprenticeship program with registered standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-102(6): "Youth apprenticeship" means a program or set of strategies that combines academic and technical classroom instruction with work experience through an apprenticeship program and which provides the foundation for youth in high school to choose among multiple pathways, including enrolling in college, beginning full-time employment, or a combination of college and employment.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103 Apprenticeship agreements -- Terms and conditions.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Every apprenticeship agreement entered into under this chapter shall contain:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103(1): the names of the contracting parties;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103(2): the date of birth of the apprentice;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103(3): a statement of the trade, craft, or business which the apprentice is to be taught, and the time at which the apprenticeship will begin;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103(4): a statement showing the number of hours to be spent by the apprentice in work and the number of hours to be spent in related and supplemental instruction, which instruction shall be not less than 144 hours per year, unless prior educational experience is substituted or prior practical experience programs are substantial as provided in other state laws;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103(5): a statement setting forth a schedule of the work processes in the trade or industry divisions in which the apprentice is to be taught and the approximate time to be spent at each process;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103(6): a statement of the graduated scale of wages to be paid the apprentice and whether the required school time shall be compensated;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103(7): a statement providing for a period of probation during which time the apprenticeship agreement may be terminated by either party to the agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-103(8): a statement that if an employer is unable to fulfill the employer's obligation under the apprenticeship agreement, the employer may transfer such obligation to another employer.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104 Application of chapter -- Voluntary election.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter applies only to such persons, firms, political subdivisions, corporations, employer associations, or bona fide organizations of employees as voluntarily elect to conform with its provisions.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104.5 Youth apprenticeships -- Workers' compensation -- Risk management.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104.5(1): As used in this section, "youth apprentice" means an individual who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104.5(1)(a): participating in a youth apprenticeship; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104.5(1)(b): enrolled in a public school.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104.5(2): 63A-4-201 A youth apprentice is considered to be a volunteer government worker of the public school in which the individual is enrolled, solely for purposes of:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104.5(2)(a): receiving workers' compensation medical benefits; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104.5(2)(b): 63A-4-201 coverage by the Risk Management Fund created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-104.5(3): (2); Title 34A, Chapter 2, Workers' Compensation Act; Chapter 3, Utah Occupational Disease Act Receipt of medical benefits under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105 Commissioner of Apprenticeship Programs.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(1): There is created the position of Commissioner of Apprenticeship Programs within the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(2): The commissioner shall be appointed by the executive director and chosen from one or more recommendations provided by a majority vote of the State Workforce Development Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(3): The commissioner may be terminated without cause by the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(4): 35A-1-109 The commissioner shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(4)(a): promote and educate the public, including high school guidance counselors and potential participants in apprenticeship programs, about apprenticeship programs, youth apprenticeship, and pre-apprenticeship programs offered in the state, including apprenticeship, youth apprenticeship, and pre-apprenticeship programs offered by private sector businesses, trade groups, labor unions, partnerships with educational institutions, and other associations in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(4)(b): coordinate with the department and other stakeholders, including union and nonunion apprenticeship programs, the Office of Apprenticeship, the State Board of Education, the Utah system of higher education, the Department of Commerce, the Division of Professional Licensing, and the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity to improve and promote apprenticeship opportunities in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(4)(c): 35A-1-109 provide an annual written report to:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(4)(c)(iii): the Higher Education Appropriations Subcommittee.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-6-105(5): (4)(c) The annual written report described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 7 - Centralized New Hire Registry Act
*******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Centralized New Hire Registry Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(1): "Business day" means a day on which state offices are open for regular business.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(2): "Compensation" means payment owed by an employer for labor or services performed by an employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(3): "Date of hire" means the date labor or services for compensation are first performed by the employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(4): "Date of rehire" means the date labor or services for compensation are first performed by an employee who was previously employed by the employer but has been separated from that employment for at least 60 consecutive days.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(5)(a): "Employee" means an individual who is an employee within the meaning of Chapter 24 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(5)(b): "Employee" does not include an employee of a federal or state agency performing intelligence or counterintelligence functions if the head of that agency determines that reporting the employee could endanger the safety of the employee or compromise an ongoing investigation or intelligence mission.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(6)(a): "Employer" means any person or entity that is an employer as defined in Section 3401(d) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(6)(b): "Employer" includes any governmental entity and any labor organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(7)(a): "Labor organization" means any entity as defined in Section 2(5) of the National Labor Relations Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(7)(b): "Labor organization" includes any entity or hiring hall that is used by agreement between the organization and an employer to carry out requirements described in Section 8(f)(3) of the National Labor Relations Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-102(8): 35A-7-103 "Registry" means the centralized new hire registry created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-103 Establishment of registry.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-103(1): 35A-7-105
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-103(1)(a): The Department of Workforce Services, through contract with the Office of Recovery Services, shall establish a centralized new hire registry database for the purpose of receiving and maintaining information on newly hired or rehired employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-103(1)(b): 35A-7-105 The database shall be formatted to conduct automatic comparisons as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-103(2): Information in the registry will be used to match the employee's employment records with other databases to allow for the rapid implementation of support orders and verification of employment status.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104 Reporting requirements.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(1): An employer that hires or rehires an employee shall send to the department:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(1)(a): the employee's name, address, Social Security number, and date of hire or date of rehire; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(1)(b): the employer's name, address, and federal tax identification number.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(2): An employer shall send the information required by this section to the department:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(2)(a): not later than 20 days after the date of hire or date of rehire; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(2)(b): if approved by the department, on a semimonthly basis of not less than 12 days nor more than 16 days apart.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(3): The department shall determine by rule the form and manner for sending the information required under this section, which may include magnetic, electronic, and voice activated transmission.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(4): The reporting requirement of this section does not apply to an employer if the employer:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(4)(a): has employees in two or more states;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(4)(b): sends the information required by this section to a state other than Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-104(4)(c): complies with the multi-state employer reporting requirement of Section 453A of the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C. 653a.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105 Requirements of the new hire registry.
----------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105(1)(a): enter the information into the registry;

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105(1)(c): when an information comparison reveals a positive match between an individual's social security number and the child support records, provide the following information to the Office of Recovery Services:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105(1)(c)(i): the name, address, and social security number of the individual; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105(1)(c)(ii): the name, address, and federal tax number of the individual's employer.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105(2): 35A-7-104 Beginning May 1, 1998, within two business days after information described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105(3): 35A-7-104 Within three business days after information described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105(4): The department shall, on a quarterly basis, furnish to the National Directory of New Hires extracts of the reports required under the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C. Sec. 303(a)(6), to be made to the Secretary of Labor concerning the wages and unemployment compensation paid to individuals by such dates, in such format, and containing such information as specified in federal regulations.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-105(5): State agencies operating employment security and workers' compensation programs may have access to the information in the registry for purposes of administering those programs.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-106 Penalties for failure to report.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-106(1): An employer who fails to timely report the hiring or rehiring of an employee as required by this chapter is subject to a civil penalty of:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-106(1)(a): $25 for each such failure; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-7-106(1)(b): $500 if the failure to report is intentional and is the result of an agreement between the employer and the employee to not supply the required information, or to supply false or incomplete information.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 8 - Housing and Community Development Division
****************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-101(1): Title 15A, State Construction and Fire Codes Act "Accessible housing" means housing which has been constructed or modified to be accessible, as described in the State Construction Code or an approved code under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-101(2): "Director" means the director of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-101(3): "Division" means the Housing and Community Development Division.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-101(4): "Moderate income housing" means housing occupied or reserved for occupancy by households with a gross household income equal to or less than 80% of the median gross income for households of the same size in the county in which the housing is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-101(5): "Moderate income housing unit" means a housing unit that qualifies as moderate income housing.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-201 Housing and Community Development Division.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Housing and Community Development Division is under the administration and general supervision of the director.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202 Powers and duties of division.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(a): assist local governments and citizens in the planning, development, and maintenance of necessary public infrastructure and services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(b): cooperate with, and provide technical assistance to, counties, cities, towns, regional planning commissions, area-wide clearinghouses, zoning commissions, parks or recreation boards, community development groups, community action agencies, and other agencies created for the purpose of aiding and encouraging an orderly, productive, and coordinated development of the state and its political subdivisions;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(c): assist the governor in coordinating the activities of state agencies which have an impact on the solution of community development problems and the implementation of community plans;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(d): serve as a clearinghouse for information, data, and other materials which may be helpful to local governments in discharging their responsibilities and provide information on available federal and state financial and technical assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(e): carry out continuing studies and analyses of the problems faced by communities within the state and develop such recommendations for administrative or legislative action as appear necessary;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(f): assist in funding affordable housing;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(g): support economic development activities through grants, loans, and direct programs financial assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(h): certify project funding at the local level in conformance with federal, state, and other requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(i): utilize the capabilities and facilities of public and private universities and colleges within the state in carrying out its functions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(1)(j): assist and support local governments, community action agencies, and citizens in the planning, development, and maintenance of home weatherization, energy efficiency, and antipoverty activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(2): Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act; Part 9, Domestic Violence Shelters; 77-36-1 The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(2)(a): Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(2)(b): if any federal program requires the expenditure of state funds as a condition to participation by the state in any fund, property, or service, with the governor's approval, expend whatever funds are necessary out of the money provided by the Legislature for the use of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(2)(c): Part 9, Domestic Violence Shelters; 77-36-1 in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-202(2)(d): assist, when requested by a county or municipality, in the development of accessible housing.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-301 Legislative intent -- Purpose and policy.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-301(1): 59-21-2 It is the intent of the Legislature to make available funds received by the state from federal mineral lease revenues under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-301(2): (1) To the extent allowed under the Mineral Leasing Act, any ambiguity as to whether a particular use of the lease revenue and bonus payments described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-301(3): The purpose of this part is to maximize the long term benefit of funds derived from these lease revenues and bonus payments by fostering funding mechanisms which will, consistent with sound financial practices, result in the greatest use of financial resources for the greatest number of citizens of this state, with priority given to those communities designated as impacted by the development of natural resources covered by the Mineral Leasing Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-301(4): The policy of this state is to promote cooperation and coordination between the state and the state's agencies and political subdivisions with individuals, firms, and business organizations engaged in the development of the natural resources of this state.
