Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-504.5(5): The executive director shall submit a report on the pilot program to the Business and Labor Interim Committee on or before November 30, 2023.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505 Activities authorized to receive fund money -- Powers of the executive director.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
At the direction of the board, the executive director may:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1): 35A-8-504.5; 35A-8-507.5 provide fund money to any of the following activities:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(a): the acquisition, rehabilitation, or new construction of low-income housing units;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(b): matching funds for social services projects directly related to providing housing for special-need renters in assisted projects;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(c): the development and construction of accessible housing designed for low-income persons;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(d): the construction or improvement of a shelter or transitional housing facility that provides services intended to prevent or minimize homelessness among members of a specific homeless subpopulation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(e): the purchase of an existing facility to provide temporary or transitional housing for the homeless in an area that does not require rezoning before providing such temporary or transitional housing;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(f): the purchase of land that will be used as the site of low-income housing units;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(g): the preservation of existing affordable housing units for low-income persons;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(h): 35A-8-504.5 providing loan guarantees under the two-year pilot program established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(i): 35A-8-507.5 the award of predevelopment grants in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(j): the creation or financial support of a mediation program for landlords and tenants designed to minimize the loss of housing for low-income persons, which program may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(j)(i): funding for the hiring or training of mediators;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(j)(ii): connecting landlords and tenants with mediation services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(j)(iii): providing a limited amount of gap funding to assist a tenant in making a good faith payment towards attorney fees, damages, or other costs associated with eviction proceedings or avoiding eviction proceedings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(1)(k): other activities that will assist in minimizing homelessness or improving the availability or quality of housing in the state for low-income persons; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(2): do any act necessary or convenient to the exercise of the powers granted by this part or reasonably implied from those granted powers, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(2)(a): making or executing contracts and other instruments necessary or convenient for the performance of the executive director and board's duties and the exercise of the executive director and board's powers and functions under this part, including contracts or agreements for the servicing and originating of mortgage loans;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(2)(b): procuring insurance against a loss in connection with property or other assets held by the fund, including mortgage loans, in amounts and from insurers it considers desirable;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(2)(c): entering into agreements with a department, agency, or instrumentality of the United States or this state and with mortgagors and mortgage lenders for the purpose of planning and regulating and providing for the financing and refinancing, purchase, construction, reconstruction, rehabilitation, leasing, management, maintenance, operation, sale, or other disposition of residential housing undertaken with the assistance of the department under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(2)(d): proceeding with a foreclosure action, to own, lease, clear, reconstruct, rehabilitate, repair, maintain, manage, operate, assign, encumber, sell, or otherwise dispose of real or personal property obtained by the fund due to the default on a mortgage loan held by the fund in preparation for disposition of the property, taking assignments of leases and rentals, proceeding with foreclosure actions, and taking other actions necessary or incidental to the performance of its duties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-505(2)(e): selling, at a public or private sale, with public bidding, a mortgage or other obligation held by the fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-506 Authority of the executive director.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
The executive director, with the approval of the board, may grant or lend fund money to a housing sponsor.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507 Application process and priorities.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(1)(a): In each calendar year that money is available from the fund for distribution by the executive director under the direction of the board, the executive director shall, at least once in that year, announce a grant and loan application period by sending notice to interested persons.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(1)(b): The executive director shall accept applications that are received in a timely manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(2): The executive director shall give priority to applications for projects and activities in the following order:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(2)(a): first, to applications for projects and activities intended to minimize homelessness;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(2)(b): second, to applications for projects and activities that use existing privately owned housing stock, including privately owned housing stock purchased by a nonprofit public development authority; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(2)(c): third, to all other applications.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3): (2) Within each level of priority described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(a): a high degree of leverage with other sources of financing;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(b): high recipient contributions to total project costs, including allied contributions from other sources such as professional, craft, and trade services and lender interest rate subsidies;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(c): high local government project contributions in the form of infrastructure improvements, or other assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(d): projects that encourage ownership, management, and other project-related responsibility opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(e): projects that demonstrate a strong probability of serving the original target group or income level for a period of at least 15 years;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(f): projects where the applicant has demonstrated the ability, stability, and resources to complete the project;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(g): projects that appear to serve the greatest need;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(h): projects that provide housing for persons and families with the lowest income;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(i): projects that promote economic development benefits;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(j): projects that align with a local government plan to address housing and homeless services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(3)(k): projects that would mitigate or correct existing health, safety, or welfare problems.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507(4): The executive director may give consideration to projects that increase the supply of accessible housing.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5 Predevelopment grants.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(1): The executive director may, under the direction of the board, award one or more predevelopment grants to a nonprofit or for-profit entity:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(1)(a): in preparation for a project that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(1)(a)(i): involves the construction of moderate income housing units; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(1)(a)(ii): is located within:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(1)(a)(ii)(A): a city of the fifth or sixth class, or a town, in a rural area of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(1)(a)(ii)(B): any municipality or unincorporated area in a county of the fourth, fifth, or sixth class; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(1)(b): in an amount of no more than $50,000 per project.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(2): The executive director shall, under the direction of the board, award each predevelopment grant in accordance with the provisions of this section and the provisions related to grant applications, grant awards, and reporting requirements in this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(3): The recipient of a predevelopment grant:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(3)(a): may use grant funds to offset the predevelopment funds needed to prepare for the construction of low-income housing units, including market studies, surveys, environmental and impact studies, technical assistance, and preliminary architecture, engineering, or legal work; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(3)(b): may not use grant funds to pay for staff salaries or construction costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(4): The executive director shall, under the direction of the board, prioritize the awarding of a predevelopment grant for a project that is located within:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(4)(a): a county of the fifth or sixth class; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(4)(b): an area that has underdeveloped infrastructure, as demonstrated by at least two of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(4)(b)(i): limited or no availability of natural gas;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(4)(b)(ii): limited or no availability of a sewer system;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(4)(b)(iii): limited or no availability of broadband Internet;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(4)(b)(iv): unpaved residential streets; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-507.5(4)(b)(v): limited local construction professionals, vendors, or services.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-508 Annual accounting.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-508(1): The executive director shall monitor the activities of recipients of grants and loans issued under this part on a yearly basis to ensure compliance with the terms and conditions imposed on the recipient by the executive director with the approval of the board or by this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-508(2): Beginning July 1, 2021, an entity that receives any money from the fund under this part shall provide the executive director with an annual accounting of how the money the entity received from the fund has been spent.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-508(3): The executive director shall make an annual report to the board accounting for the expenditures authorized by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-508(4): 35A-1-109 The board shall submit a report to the department for inclusion in the annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-508(4)(a): accounting for expenditures authorized by the board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-508(4)(b): evaluating the effectiveness of the program.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-511 Activities authorized to receive account money.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The executive director may distribute funds from the Economic Revitalization and Investment Fund and the Rural Housing Fund for any of the following activities undertaken as part of an approved project:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-511(1): the acquisition, rehabilitation, or new construction of a building that includes moderate income housing units;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-511(2): the purchase of land for the construction of a building that will include moderate income housing units; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-511(3): pre-development work, including planning, studies, design, and site work for a building that will include moderate income housing units.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-801 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Housing Coordination and Planning Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802 Legislative policy and purpose.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(1)(a): The Legislature declares that it is the policy of the state that to promote the general welfare of its citizens it is necessary to remedy the unsafe and unsanitary housing conditions and the acute shortage of decent, safe, and sanitary dwellings for families of medium and low income, in urban and rural areas.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(1)(b): (1)(a) The conditions described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2): 70D-2-102 The Legislature declares that it is the policy of the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a): 70D-2-102 to make adequate provision of affordable housing for:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(i): 70D-2-102 persons of medium or low income who are unable to provide themselves with decent housing including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(i)(A): elderly persons;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(i)(B): persons with disabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(i)(C): veterans;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(i)(D): special needs populations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(i)(E): low income persons living on tribal trust lands;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(i)(F): persons receiving public assistance under self-sufficiency programs; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(i)(G): 70D-2-102 low income persons living in mobile homes, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(a)(ii): during limited periods, for disaster victims; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(2)(b): that the provision of safe and sanitary dwelling accommodations at rents or prices that persons of medium and low income can afford will materially assist in developing more desirable neighborhoods and alleviating the effects of poverty in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(3): Part 4, Housing Authorities The purposes of this part and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(3)(a): providing low-cost housing for medium and low income persons; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(3)(b): encouraging cooperation between political subdivisions and the nonprofit sector to make available low-cost housing in all areas of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4): 70D-2-102 It is in the public interest to use the broad financial resources and technical services available to government in cooperation with the ingenuity and expertise of private enterprise to alleviate this lack of safe and sanitary dwellings while stimulating local industry, according to the following principles:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(a): The private sector, including nonprofit entities, shall be the primary source of developing and providing affordable housing with state and local incentives to encourage housing development.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b): 70D-2-102 State money used in the development of housing shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(i): be heavily leveraged when possible;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(ii): be primarily invested as loans;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iii): be primarily spent on housing production; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iv): 70D-2-102 give priority to needs of persons of medium or low income who are unable to provide themselves with decent housing including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iv)(A): elderly persons;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iv)(B): persons with disabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iv)(C): veterans;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iv)(D): special needs populations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iv)(E): low income persons living on tribal trust lands;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iv)(F): persons receiving public assistance under self-sufficiency programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(b)(iv)(G): 70D-2-102 low income persons living in mobile homes, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(c): When possible based on economic feasibility and effectiveness, state housing programs shall encourage:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(c)(i): mixed income developments;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(c)(ii): socio-economic diversity in neighborhoods; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(c)(iii): new, multifamily construction.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(d): State resources may be used in partnership with political subdivisions or the private sector to promote affordable housing.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-802(4)(e): Within appropriations from the Legislature, the state may provide training and technical assistance to Utah's political subdivision, quasi-governmental, and nonprofit housing providers.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-803 Division -- Functions.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-803(1): (1)(a)(iii); 10-9a-408; 17-27a-408; 10-9a-408; 17-27a-408; 10-9a-403; 17-27a-403 In addition to any other functions the governor or Legislature may assign:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-803(1)(a): (1)(a)(iii); 10-9a-408; 17-27a-408; 10-9a-408; 17-27a-408; 10-9a-403; 17-27a-403 the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-803(1)(a)(i): provide a clearinghouse of information for federal, state, and local housing assistance programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-803(1)(a)(ii): establish, in cooperation with political subdivisions, model plans and management methods to encourage or provide for the development of affordable housing that may be adopted by political subdivisions by reference;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-803(1)(a)(iii): undertake, in cooperation with political subdivisions, a realistic assessment of problems relating to housing needs, such as:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-803(1)(a)(iii)(A): inadequate supply of dwellings;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-803(1)(a)(iii)(B): substandard dwellings; and

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805 Reporting requirements.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(1)(a): "Affordable housing" means, as determined by the department, the number of housing units within a county or municipality where a household whose income is at or below 50% of area median income is able to live in a unit without spending more than 30% of their income on housing costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(1)(b): "County" means the unincorporated area of a county.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(1)(c): "Low-income housing" means, as determined by the department, the number of Section 42, Internal Revenue Code, housing units within a county or municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(1)(d): "Municipality" means a city, town, or metro township.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(2): 35A-1-109
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(2)(a): 35A-1-109 On or before October 1 of each year, the division shall provide a report to the department for inclusion in the department's annual report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(2)(b): The report shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(2)(b)(i): an estimate of how many affordable housing units and how many low-income housing units are available in each county and municipality in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(2)(b)(ii): a determination of the percentage of affordable housing available in each county and municipality in the state as compared to the statewide average;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(2)(b)(iii): a determination of the percentage of low-income housing available in each county and municipality in the state as compared to the statewide average; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-805(2)(b)(iv): a description of how information in the report was calculated.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1001 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as the "State Community Services Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(1): "Community action agency" means a local subdivision of the state, a combination of political subdivisions, a separate public agency, or a private nonprofit agency, which:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(1)(a): has the authority under its applicable charter or laws to receive funds to support community action activities and other appropriate measures designed to identify and deal with the causes of poverty in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(1)(b): is designated as a community action agency by federal law, federal regulations, or the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(2): "Community action program budget" means state funds, federal block grants, and federal categorical grants that are received by the state for community action activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(3): "Community action statewide organization" means community action programs, organized on a statewide basis, to enhance the capability of community action agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(4): "Community Services Block Grant" means the Federal Community Services Block Grant Act, 42 U.S.C. Sec. 9901 et seq., and any corresponding federal regulations.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(5): "Local share" means cash or in-kind goods and services donated to a community action agency to carry out its responsibilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(6): "Low-income person" means a person who is a member of a household with a gross annual income equal to or less than 125% of the poverty standard accepted by the federal agency designated to establish poverty guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(7): 35A-8-1003 "Office" means the State Community Services Office created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1002(8): "Service area" means the geographical area within the jurisdiction of a community action agency or a community action statewide organization.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1003 State Community Services Office created -- Purpose.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1003(1): There is created within the Housing and Community Development Division the State Community Services Office.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1003(2): The office shall strengthen communities by reducing poverty and improving the quality of life for low-income persons in this state.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004 Duties of office.
--------------------------------------------------
The office shall:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(1): coordinate state activities designed to reduce poverty;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(2): encourage entities in the private sector to participate in efforts to ameliorate poverty in the community;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(3): cooperate with agencies of local, state, and the federal government in reducing poverty and implementing community, social, and economic programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(4): receive and expend funds for the purposes outlined in this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(5): enter into contracts with and award grants to public and private nonprofit agencies and organizations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(6): develop a state plan based on needs identified by community action agencies and community action statewide organizations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(7): designate community action agencies to receive funds through the Community Services Block Grant program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(8): fund community action agencies and community action statewide organizations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(9): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act make rules in conjunction with the division in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(10): provide assistance to local governments or private organizations for the purpose of establishing and operating a community action agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(11): provide technical assistance to community action agencies to improve program planning, program development, administration, and the mobilization of public and private resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(12): convene public meetings that provide citizens the opportunity to comment on public policies and programs to reduce poverty;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(13): advise the governor and Legislature of the nature and extent of poverty in the state and make recommendations concerning changes in state and federal policies and programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(14): encourage Utah's nonprofit humanitarian assistance agencies serving low-income persons by facilitating, coordinating, training, and providing technical assistance to address the needs of Utah's low-income persons by enhancing management, improving service and program delivery, facilitating partnerships, and preserving flexibility and local initiative;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(15): develop and implement management goals that fulfill the Community Services Block Grant mission, state requirements, and the mandates of federal legislation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(16): prepare a Community Services Block Grant plan that contains provisions describing how the state will carry out the assurances of the Community Services Block Grant Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(17): act as the state agency responsible for the evaluation and improvement of emergency food assistance services in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(18): monitor the impact of social policies on the emergency food network;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(19): provide training and technical assistance to grantees to assist their:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(19)(a): program development and implementation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(19)(b): compliance with state and federal regulations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(19)(c): reporting and management information systems;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(20): 35A-8-1009 make the distributions required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1004(21): administer other programs to alleviate poverty that are assigned to the office.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1005 Distribution of Community Services Block Grant funds.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Community Services Block Grant funds received by the office shall be distributed as follows:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1005(1): 90% to community action agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1005(2): 5% to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1005(2)(a): organizations with a statewide focus to accomplish specific objectives that complement the Community Services Block Grant poverty programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1005(2)(b): provide training and technical assistance for grantees of Community Services Block Grant funds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1005(2)(c): supplement anti-poverty projects; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1005(3): 5% to reimburse costs incurred by the office in administration of this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006 Evaluations -- Reports.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The office shall periodically evaluate grantees of Community Services Block Grant funds as established by rule by the division in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006(2): A grantee of Community Services Block Grant funds shall submit to the office a year-end report, covering a reporting period consistent with the federal fiscal year, which provides an account of the grantee's programs operated with or supported by Community Services Block Grant funds, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006(2)(a): the types of programs operated by the grantee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006(2)(b): the outcome of each program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006(2)(c): the number of persons served by each program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006(2)(d): the number of times service was given by each program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006(2)(e): an accounting of the Community Services Block Grant funds expended by the grantee.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1006(3): The office shall report annually to the appropriate legislative appropriations subcommittee on the distribution and expenditure of Community Services Block Grant funds.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007 Program development by grantees.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Grantees of Community Services Block Grant funds shall develop specific programs and goals, consistent with the Community Services Block Grant Act, designed to provide the most effective solutions to the problems of poverty identified in their communities within the constraints of available funding, including projects related to:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(1): employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(2): education;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(3): income management;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(4): housing;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(5): emergency assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(6): nutrition;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(7): linkages and coordination with other programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(8): health; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1007(9): self-sufficiency.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1008 Recognition of community action agencies.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
The office may:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1008(1): recognize eligible organizations as community action agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1008(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act withdraw the recognition or terminate funding of a designated community action agency for cause, as established by rule made by the division in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1008(3): change the boundaries and the number of recognized community action agencies, provided that the governing board of each affected community action agency concurs in the action.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1401 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Home Energy Assistance Target (HEAT) Program Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1402 Assistance to low-income persons -- Contracts -- Administration.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1402(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1402(1)(a): The department may assist certain low-income families and individuals in the payment of home energy costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1402(1)(b): Assistance given under this part shall be made available to households throughout the state, irrespective of the source of household energy supply.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1402(2): The department may contract with one or more public or private agencies to distribute and administer these funds subject to the criteria established by the department.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1403 Eligibility criteria.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1403(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1403(2): A recipient of assistance under this part shall demonstrate:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1403(2)(a): that the recipient's family, household, or individual income is 150% of the federal poverty level or less;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1403(2)(b): that the recipient is responsible for paying the recipient's home energy costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1403(2)(c): compliance with any rules established by the department under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1404 Guidelines for private contributions -- Assuring equitable distribution.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department shall coordinate with private contributors to home energy assistance programs, such as REACH and Lend-a-Hand, to help assure equitable statewide distribution of assistance to eligible customers of all vendors of energy services.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1405 Payment method.
------------------------------------------------
Direct payments for home energy costs shall be made jointly to the responsible householder and to the vendor of energy services to whom the family or individual served owes a payment except in certain cases, as established by rule by the department in accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501 Moratorium on involuntary termination for nonpayment of utility bills -- Eligibility criteria -- Department to establish and certify.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(1): Title 54, Public Utilities
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(1)(a): The department shall establish a program for a seasonal moratorium for involuntary termination for nonpayment by residential customers of essential utility bills.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(1)(b): Title 54, Public Utilities An essential utility is a utility regulated by the Public Service Commission under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(1)(c): A residential customer is a customer defined as in a residential class by the Public Service Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(2): A residential customer shall meet the following criteria to qualify for the program:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(2)(a): gross household income is less than 125% of the federal poverty level or the household has suffered a medical or other emergency, loss of employment, or is experiencing other circumstances which have resulted in a substantial loss of income;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(2)(b): the customer has made application to public and private energy assistance programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(2)(c): the customer is willing to make a good faith effort to pay these utility bills on a consistent basis; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(2)(d): any additional information required by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(3): (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(3)(a): (2) A residential customer may file with a local department office an affidavit attesting eligibility under the criteria in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1501(3)(b): The department shall certify that the customer has met the eligibility requirements and forward a copy of the affidavit to the effected utility.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1502 Contesting a customer's eligibility -- Department to determine case.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
When a utility contests the eligibility of any residential customer to participate in the program, the executive director or the executive director's designee shall act as an administrative law judge to make a determination on the case.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1503 Premoratorium customers' eligibility for moratorium -- Criteria.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A residential customer that has had service of an essential utility discontinued for nonpayment prior to the time the moratorium takes effect shall have service restored and continued during the period of the moratorium if the customer meets the requirements of Section

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1504 Effective period of moratorium -- Extension by rule.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1504(1): The moratorium shall be in effect from November 15 to March 15 of each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1504(2): The department may, by rule, begin the moratorium at an earlier date or extend it to a later date when severe weather conditions warrant that action.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601(1): "Board" means the Uintah Basin Revitalization Fund Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601(2): "Capital projects" means expenditures for land, improvements on the land, and equipment intended to have long-term beneficial use.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601(3): "County" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601(3)(a): Duchesne County; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601(3)(b): Uintah County.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601(4): "Division" means the Housing and Community Development Division.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601(5): "Revitalization Fund" means the Uintah Basin Revitalization Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1601(6): "Tribe" means the Ute Indian Tribe of the Uintah and Ouray Reservation.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1602 Legislative intent -- Uintah Basin Revitalization Fund -- Deposits and contents.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1602(1): In order to maximize the long-term benefit of severance taxes derived from lands held in trust by the United States for the Tribe and its members by fostering funding mechanisms that will, consistent with sound financial practices, result in the greatest use of financial resources for the greatest number of citizens of the Uintah Basin, and in order to promote cooperation and coordination between the state, its political subdivisions, Indian tribes, and individuals, firms, and business organizations engaged in the development of oil and gas interests held in trust for the Tribe and its members, there is created an expendable special revenue fund entitled the "Uintah Basin Revitalization Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1602(2): 59-5-116 The fund consists of all money deposited to the Revitalization Fund under this part and Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1602(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1602(3)(a): The Revitalization Fund shall earn interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1602(3)(b): All interest earned on fund money shall be deposited into the fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603 Uintah Basin Revitalization Fund Board created -- Members -- Terms -- Chair -- Quorum -- Expenses.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(1): There is created within the division the Revitalization Board composed of five members as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(1)(a): the governor or his designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(1)(b): a Uintah County commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(1)(c): a Duchesne County commissioner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(1)(d): two representatives of the Business Committee of the Tribe.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(2): The terms of office for the members of the board shall run concurrently with the terms of office for the governor, commissioners, and Business Committee of the Tribe.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(3): The governor, or his designee, shall be the chair of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(4): Four board members are a quorum.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(5): All decisions of the board require four affirmative votes.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(6): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(6)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(6)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1603(6)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606 Eligibility for assistance -- Applications -- Review by board -- Terms -- Security.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(1): Counties or the Tribe that wish to receive loans or grants from the board shall submit formal applications to the board containing the information required by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(2): The board may not fund:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(2)(a): start-up or operational costs of private business ventures; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(2)(b): general operating budgets of the counties or the Tribe, except that the Tribe may use a grant or loan to fund costs associated with the management and administration of energy or mineral development on:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(2)(b)(i): lands held in trust by the United States for the Tribe and its members; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(2)(b)(ii): lands owned by the Tribe.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(3)(a): The board shall review each application for a loan or grant before approving it.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(3)(b): The board may approve loan or grant applications subject to the applicant's compliance with certain conditions established by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(3)(c): The board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(3)(c)(i): ensure that each loan specifies the terms for repayment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1606(3)(c)(ii): secure the loans by proceeds from any general obligation, special assessment, or revenue bonds, notes, or other obligations of the appropriate subdivision.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1607 Division to distribute money -- Annual report -- Administration costs.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1607(1): The division shall distribute loan and grant money if the loan or grant is approved by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1607(2): 35A-1-109 The division shall provide an annual report to the department concerning the number and type of loans and grants made as well as a list of recipients of this assistance for inclusion in the department's annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1607(3): The division, with board approval, may use fund money for the administration of the fund, but this amount may not exceed 2% of the annual receipts to the fund.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1701 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Navajo Revitalization Fund Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(1): "Board" means the Navajo Revitalization Fund Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(2): "Capital project" means an expenditure for land, improvements on the land, or equipment intended to have long-term beneficial use.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(3): "Division" means the Housing and Community Development Division.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(4): "Eligible entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(4)(a): the Navajo Nation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(4)(b): a department or division of the Navajo Nation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(4)(c): a Utah Navajo Chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(4)(d): the Navajo Utah Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(4)(e): an agency of the state or a political subdivision of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(4)(f): a nonprofit corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(5): "Navajo Utah Commission" means the commission created by Resolution IGRJN-134-92 of the Intergovernmental Relations Committee of the Navajo Nation Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(6): "Revitalization fund" means the Navajo Revitalization Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(7): "Utah Navajo Chapter" means any of the following chapters of the Navajo Nation:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(7)(a): Aneth Chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(7)(b): Dennehotso Chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(7)(c): Mexican Water Chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(7)(d): Navajo Mountain Chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(7)(e): Oljato Chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(7)(f): Red Mesa Chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1702(7)(g): Teec Nos Pos Chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1703 Legislative intent.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1703(1): The purpose of this part is to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1703(1)(a): maximize the long-term benefit of state severance taxes derived from lands in Utah held in trust by the United States for the Navajo Nation and its members by fostering funding mechanisms that will, consistent with sound financial practices, result in the greatest use of financial resources for the greatest number of citizens of San Juan County; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1703(1)(b): promote cooperation and coordination between the state, its political subdivisions, Indian tribes, and individuals, firms, and business organizations engaged in the development of oil and gas interests in Utah held in trust by the United States for the Navajo Nation and its members.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1703(2): (1) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1703(2)(a): consists of state severance tax money to be spent at the discretion of the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1703(2)(b): does not constitute a trust fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704 Navajo Revitalization Fund.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(1): 59-5-119
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(1)(a): There is created an expendable special revenue fund called the "Navajo Revitalization Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(1)(b): 59-5-119 The revitalization fund shall consist of:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(1)(b)(i): money deposited to the revitalization fund under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(1)(b)(ii): 59-5-119 money deposited to the revitalization fund under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(1)(b)(iii): any loan repayment or interest on a loan issued under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(2)(a): The revitalization fund shall earn interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(2)(b): The interest earned on revitalization fund money shall be deposited into the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1704(3): Beginning for fiscal year 2010-11, the division may use revitalization fund money for the administration of the revitalization fund, but this amount may not exceed 4% of the annual receipts to the revitalization fund.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1705(1)(d)(ii): 35A-8-1702(7) the Utah Navajo Chapter is rotated in alphabetical order as provided in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1705(1)(d)(iii)(B): the president of the next Utah Navajo Chapter in the alphabetical rotation shall serve on the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1705(2): (1)(a); (c) The term of office for a member of the board described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1705(3):

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1705(4)(a): 63A-3-106 Section

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707 Revitalization fund administered by board -- Eligibility for assistance -- Review by board -- Restrictions on loans and grants -- Division to distribute money.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(1)(a): If an eligible entity wishes to receive a loan or grant from the board, the eligible entity shall file an application with the board that contains the information required by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(1)(b): (1)(a) The board shall review an application for a loan or grant filed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(1)(c): The board may approve a loan or grant application subject to the applicant's compliance with the one or more conditions established by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2): In determining whether an eligible entity may receive a loan or grant, the board shall give priority to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(a): a capital project or infrastructure, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(a)(i): electrical power;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(a)(ii): water; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(a)(iii): a one time need project;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(b): a housing project that consists of:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(b)(i): the purchase of new housing;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(b)(ii): the construction of new housing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(b)(iii): a significant remodeling of existing housing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(c): a matching educational endowment that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(c)(i): promotes economic development within the Utah portion of the Navajo Reservation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(c)(ii): promotes the preservation of Navajo culture, history, and language; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(2)(c)(iii): supports a postsecondary educational opportunity for a Navajo student enrolled in a course or program taught within the Utah portion of the Navajo Reservation.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(3): (2)(c) A loan or grant issued under this part may not fund:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(3)(a): a start-up or operational cost of a private business venture;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(3)(b): a general operating budget of an eligible entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(3)(c): (2)(c) a project that will operate or be located outside of the Navajo Reservation in San Juan County, Utah, except for an educational endowment approved by the board under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(4)(a): The board may not approve a loan unless the loan:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(4)(a)(i): specifies the terms for repayment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(4)(a)(ii): is secured by proceeds from a general obligation, special assessment, or revenue bond, note, or other obligation.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(4)(b): The division shall deposit a loan repayment or interest on a loan issued under this part into the revitalization fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(5): The board shall give a priority to a loan or grant if the loan or grant includes matching money or in-kind services from:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(5)(a): the Navajo Nation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(5)(b): San Juan County;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(5)(c): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(5)(d): the federal government;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(5)(e): a Utah Navajo Chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(5)(f): other private or public organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(6): 63A-3-205 The division shall distribute loan and grant money:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(6)(a): if the loan or grant is approved by the board;

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-1707(6)(b)(i): inconsistent with this part; or

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2101 Title -- Purpose.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2101(1): This part is known as "Private Activity Bonds."
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2101(2): This part establishes procedures to effectively and equitably allocate this state's private activity bond volume cap authorized by the Internal Revenue Code of 1986 in order to maximize the social and economic benefits to this state.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(1): "Allocated volume cap" means a volume cap for which:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(1)(a): a certificate of allocation is in effect; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(1)(b): bonds have been issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(2): 35A-8-2106 "Allotment accounts" means the various accounts created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(3): 35A-8-2103 "Board of review" means the Private Activity Bond Review Board created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(4): "Bond" means any obligation for which an allocation of volume cap is required by the code.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(5): "Code" means the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended, and any related Internal Revenue Service regulations.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(6): "Form 8038" means the Department of the Treasury tax form 8038 (OMB No. 1545-0720) or any other federal tax form or other method of reporting required by the Department of the Treasury under Section 149(e) of the code.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(7): "Issuing authority" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(7)(a): any county, city, or town in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(7)(b): any not-for-profit corporation or joint agency, or other entity acting on behalf of one or more counties, cities, towns, or any combination of these;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(7)(c): the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(7)(d): any other entity authorized to issue bonds under state law.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(8): "State" means the state of Utah and any of its agencies, institutions, and divisions authorized to issue bonds or certificates under state law.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(9): "Volume cap" means the private activity bond volume cap for the state as computed under Section 146 of the code.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2102(10): "Year" means each calendar year.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104 Powers, functions, and duties of the board of review.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The board of review shall:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104(1): make, subject to the limitations of the code, allocations of volume cap to issuing authorities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104(2): determine the amount of volume cap to be allocated with respect to approved applications;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104(3): 35A-8-2105; 35A-8-2107 maintain a record of all applications filed by issuing authorities under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104(4): maintain a record of all bonds issued by issuing authorities during each year;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104(5): determine the amount of volume cap to be treated as a carryforward under Section 146(f) of the code and allocate this carryforward to one or more qualified carryforward purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104(6): make available upon reasonable request a certified copy of all or any part of the records maintained by the board of review under this part or a summary of them, including information relating to the volume cap for each year and any amounts available for allocation under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104(7): make rules for the allocation of volume cap under this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2104(8): charge reasonable fees for the performance of duties prescribed by this part, including application, filing, and processing fees.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105 Allocation of volume cap.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(1): (1)(b); 35A-8-2106; 35A-8-2106
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(1)(a): (1)(b); 35A-8-2106 Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(1)(b): 35A-8-2106 The board of review may distribute up to 50% of each increase in the volume cap for use in development that occurs in quality growth areas, depending upon the board's analysis of the relative need for additional volume cap between development in quality growth areas and the allotment accounts under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(2): To obtain an allocation of the volume cap, issuing authorities shall submit to the board of review an application containing information required by the procedures and processes of the board of review.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(a): The board of review shall establish criteria for making allocations of volume cap that are consistent with the purposes of the code and this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b): In making an allocation of volume cap the board of review shall consider the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(i): the principal amount of the bonds proposed to be issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(ii): the nature and the location of the project or the type of program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(iii): the likelihood that the bonds will be sold and the timeframe of bond issuance;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(iv): whether the project or program could obtain adequate financing without an allocation of volume cap;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(v): the degree to which an allocation of volume cap is required for the project or program to proceed or continue;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(vi): the social, health, economic, and educational effects of the project or program on the local community and state as a whole;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(vii): the anticipated economic development created or retained within the local community and the state as a whole;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(viii): the anticipated number of jobs, both temporary and permanent, created or retained within the local community and the state as a whole; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(ix): if the project is a residential rental project, the degree to which the residential rental project:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(ix)(A): targets lower income populations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(3)(b)(ix)(B): is accessible housing.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(4): 35A-8-2107 The board of review shall provide evidence of an allocation of volume cap by issuing a certificate in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(5): (5)(c); (5)(c); 35A-8-2106(2)(c); (5)(a); (b)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(5)(a): (5)(c) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(5)(b): (5)(c) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2105(5)(c): 35A-8-2106(2)(c); (5)(a); (b) The board of review is not required to set aside any unused volume cap under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106 Allotment accounts.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1): (1)(a); (b); (c) There are created the following allotment accounts:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(a): the Single Family Housing Account, for which eligible issuing authorities are those authorized under the code and state statute to issue qualified mortgage bonds under Section 143 of the code;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(b): the Student Loan Account, for which eligible issuing authorities are those authorized under the code and state statute to issue qualified student loan bonds under Section 144(b) of the code;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(c): the Small Issue Bond Account, for which eligible issuing authorities are those authorized under the code and state statute to issue:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(c)(i): qualified small issue bonds under Section 144(a) of the code;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(c)(ii): qualified exempt facility bonds for qualified residential rental projects under Section 142(d) of the code; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(c)(iii): qualified redevelopment bonds under Section 144(c) of the code;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(d): (1)(a); (b); (c) the Exempt Facilities Account, for which eligible issuing authorities are those authorized under the code and state statute to issue any bonds requiring an allocation of volume cap other than for purposes described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(e): the Pool Account, for which eligible issuing authorities are those authorized under the code and state statute to issue any bonds requiring an allocation of volume cap; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(1)(f): the Carryforward Account, for which eligible issuing authorities are those with projects or programs qualifying under Section 146(f) of the code.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(a): The volume cap shall be distributed to the allotment accounts on January 1 of each year on the following basis:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(a)(i): 42% to the Single Family Housing Account;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(a)(ii): 33% to the Student Loan Account;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(a)(iii): 1% to the Exempt Facilities Account; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(a)(iv): 24% to the Small Issue Bond Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(b): From July 1 to September 30 of each year, the board of review may transfer any unallocated volume cap from the Exempt Facilities Account or the Small Issue Bond Account to the Pool Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(c): Upon written notification by the issuing authorities eligible for volume cap allocation from the Single Family Housing Account or the Student Loan Account that all or a portion of volume cap distributed into that allotment account will not be used, the board of review may transfer the unused volume cap to any other allotment account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(d): From October 1 to the third Friday of December of each year, the board of review shall transfer all unallocated volume cap into the Pool Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(e): On the third Saturday of December of each year, the board of review shall transfer uncollected volume cap, or allocated volume cap for which bonds have not been issued prior to the third Saturday of December, into the Carryforward Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2106(2)(f): If the authority to issue bonds designated in any allotment account is rescinded by amendment to the code, the board of review may transfer any unallocated volume cap from that allotment account to any other allotment account.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107 Certificates of allocation.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(1)(a): After an allocation of volume cap for a project or program is approved by the board of review, the board of review shall issue a numbered certificate of allocation stating the amount of the allocation, the allotment account for which the allocation is being made, and the expiration date of the allocation.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(1)(b): The certificates of allocation shall be mailed to the issuing authority within 10 working days of the date of approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(1)(c): Bonds are not entitled to any allocation of the volume cap unless the issuing authority received a certificate of allocation with respect to the bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(1)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(1)(d)(i): Certificates of allocation shall remain in effect for a period of 90 days from the date of approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(1)(d)(ii): If bonds for which a certificate has been approved are not issued within the 90-day period, the certificate of allocation is void and volume cap shall be returned to the applicable allotment account for reallocation by the board of review.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(2): (1); (2)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(2)(a): (1) An issuing authority receiving an allocation of volume cap from the Carryforward Account shall receive a certificate of allocation similar to the certificates of allocation described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(2)(b): (2)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(2)(b)(i): If in the judgment of the board of review an issuing authority or a person or entity responsible for a project or program receiving an allocation from the Carryforward Account does not proceed with diligence in providing for the issuance of the bonds with respect to the project or program, and because of the lack of diligence the volume cap cannot be used, the board of review may exclude from the board of review's consideration for a given period of time, determined by the board of review, an application of the issuing authority, person, or entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2107(2)(b)(ii): (2)(b) The board of review may, at any time, review and modify the board of review's decisions relating to the exclusion described in this Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201(1): 35A-8-2202 "Commission" means the Commission on Housing Affordability created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201(2): "Housing affordability" means the ability of a household to occupy a housing unit paying no more than 30% of the household's income for gross housing costs, including utilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201(3): "Moderate income housing unit" means a housing unit where a household whose income is no more than 80% of the area median income is able to occupy the housing unit paying no more than 30% of the household's income for gross housing costs, including utilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201(4): "Replacement unit" means a moderate income housing unit that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201(4)(a): is comparable in quality to a permanently vacated or destroyed moderate income housing unit;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201(4)(b): meets state and local health and housing codes;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201(4)(c): is comparable to the permanently vacated or destroyed moderate income housing unit in number of bedrooms and square footage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2201(4)(d): is located, to the extent practicable, in the same political subdivision as the permanently vacated or destroyed moderate income housing unit.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2203 Duties of the commission.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2203(1): 63N-1a-202; 35A-8-803(1)(a)(ix) The commission shall:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2203(1)(d): facilitate the communication and coordination of public and private entities that are involved in developing, financing, providing, advocating for, and administering affordable housing in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2203(1)(e): study, evaluate, and report on the status and effectiveness of policies, procedures, and programs that address housing affordability in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2203(1)(f): study and evaluate the policies, procedures, and programs implemented by other states that address housing affordability;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2203(1)(g): provide a forum for public comment on issues related to housing affordability;

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-8-2203(1)(i): 35A-8-803(1)(a)(ix) on or before December 31, 2022, approve the methodology developed by the division under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 9 - Intergenerational Poverty Mitigation Act
**************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Intergenerational Poverty Mitigation Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102(1): "Cycle of poverty" or "poverty cycle" means the set of factors or events by which the long-term poverty of a person is likely to continue and be experienced by each child of the person when the child becomes an adult unless there is outside intervention.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102(2)(a): "Intergenerational poverty" means poverty in which two or more successive generations of a family continue in the cycle of poverty and government dependance.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102(2)(b): "Intergenerational poverty" does not include situational poverty.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102(3): "Poverty" means the state of a person who lacks a usual or socially acceptable amount of money or material possessions as demonstrated by the person's income level being at or below the United States poverty level as defined by the most recently revised poverty income guidelines published by the United States Department of Health and Human Services in the Federal Register.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102(4): "Situational poverty" means temporary poverty that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102(4)(a): is generally traceable to a specific incident or time period within the lifetime of a person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-102(4)(b): is not continued to the next generation.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201 Intergenerational poverty tracking system -- Data -- Analysis.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(1): The department shall establish and maintain a system to track intergenerational poverty.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2): The system shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(a): identify groups that have a high risk of experiencing intergenerational poverty;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(b): identify incidents, patterns, and trends that explain or contribute to intergenerational poverty;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(c): assist case workers, social scientists, and government officials in the study and development of effective and efficient plans and programs to help individuals and families in the state to break the cycle of poverty; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(d): gather and track available local, state, and national data on:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(d)(i): official poverty rates;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(d)(ii): child poverty rates;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(d)(iii): years spent by individuals in childhood poverty;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(d)(iv): years spent by individuals in adult poverty; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(2)(d)(v): related poverty information.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(3): (2); Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act The department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(3)(a): use available data in the tracking system, including public assistance data, census data, and other data made available to the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(3)(b): (2) develop and implement methods to integrate, compare, analyze, and validate the data for the purposes described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(3)(c): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act protect the privacy of individuals living in poverty by using and distributing data within the tracking system in compliance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(3)(c)(i): federal requirements; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-201(3)(c)(ii): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act the provisions of

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-202(2)(a): 35A-9-201 report on the data, findings, and potential uses of the intergenerational poverty tracking system described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-202(2)(b): describe policies, procedures, and programs that the department has implemented or modified to help break the cycle of poverty and end welfare dependency for children in the state affected by intergenerational poverty;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-202(2)(c): contain recommendations to the Legislature on how to address issues relating to breaking the cycle of poverty and ending welfare dependency for children in the state affected by intergenerational poverty; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-202(2)(d): 9-1-210; 26B-1-218; 53E-1-206 include the following reports:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(1): "529 savings account" means a tax-advantaged method of saving for higher education costs that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(1)(a): meets the requirements of Section 529, Internal Revenue Code; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(1)(b): is managed by the plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(2): "Beneficiary" means the individual designated:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(2)(a): in a 529 savings account agreement between a person, an estate, or a trust and the plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(2)(b): to benefit from the amount saved in a 529 savings account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(3): "Commission" means the State Tax Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(4): "Deposit" means the payment of money from a source other than a match.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(5): "Eligible 529 savings account" means a 529 savings account for which:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(5)(a): a qualifying individual is the account owner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(5)(b): a qualifying individual or a minor dependent of a qualifying individual is a beneficiary.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(6): "Federal earned income tax credit" means the federal earned income tax credit:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(6)(a): described in Section 32, Internal Revenue Code; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(6)(b): that a qualifying individual claims and is eligible to claim on the federal income tax return for the taxable year.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(7): 35A-9-603(2) "Match" means the monetary amount described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(8): "Minor dependent" means an individual under 19 years old for whom a qualifying individual can claim a tax credit under Section 24, Internal Revenue Code, on the qualifying individual's federal income tax return for the taxable year.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(9): 53B-8a-103 "Plan" means the Utah Educational Savings Plan created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(10): 35A-9-603 "Program" means the Education Savings Incentive Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-601(11): "Qualifying individual" means an individual who the department identifies as experiencing intergenerational poverty and who has not been disqualified from participating in the program for overclaiming a match in a previous year.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602 Education Savings Incentive Restricted Account.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(1): There is created a restricted account within the Income Tax Fund to be known as the Education Savings Incentive Restricted Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(2): The department shall administer the restricted account for the purposes described in this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(3): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer shall invest the money in the restricted account according to the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(4): The restricted account shall be funded by:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(4)(a): appropriations made to the account by the Legislature; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(4)(b): private donations, grants, gifts, bequests, or money made available from any other source to implement this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(5): Subject to appropriation, the department:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(5)(a): shall use restricted account money for the program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-602(5)(b): may use a portion of the restricted account money for administration of the program.
