Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605 Payment of match.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605(1): Subject to the other provisions of this section, the department shall transfer money appropriated from the Education Savings Incentive Restricted Account to the plan in the amount of each qualifying individual's match.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605(2): (1) The department shall send with the transfer described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605(2)(a): the amount of the match for the qualifying individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605(2)(b): the qualifying individual's allocation of the match among eligible 529 savings accounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605(2)(c): for each eligible 529 savings account into which the qualifying individual allocates the match:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605(2)(c)(i): the name of the qualifying individual who is the account owner;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605(2)(c)(ii): the name of the beneficiary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-605(2)(c)(iii): the account number.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606 Reporting to the department -- Annual report.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(1): On or before September 1, the plan shall submit to the department the aggregate average balance in eligible 529 savings accounts during the previous calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(2): 35A-1-109 The department shall include in the annual report required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(2)(a): the number of qualifying individuals to whom the department provides notice of the program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(2)(b): the number of applications for the program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(2)(c): the number of applications for the program from qualifying individuals;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(2)(d): the number of qualifying individuals participating in the program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(2)(e): the number of eligible 529 savings accounts that receive a match;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(2)(f): the total dollar amount provided as a match; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-9-606(2)(g): the aggregate average balance in eligible 529 savings accounts as reported by the plan.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 12 - Achieving a Better Life Experience Program Act
*********************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Achieving a Better Life Experience Program Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-102(1): "Account" means  an account in a qualified ABLE program.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-102(2): "Qualified ABLE program" means the same as that term is defined in 26 U.S.C. Sec. 529A.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-102(3): "State Achieving a Better Life Experience Program" means the program created by this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201 Creation of program.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(1): There is created the state Achieving a Better Life Experience Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(2): The department shall do one of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(2)(a): administer the state Achieving a Better Life Experience Program in compliance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(2)(a)(i): 26 U.S.C. Sec. 529A; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(2)(a)(ii): regulations, if any, issued by the United States Department of the Treasury;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(2)(b): enter into a contract with a state that maintains a qualified ABLE program to provide Utah residents access to that state's qualified ABLE program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(2)(c): inform eligible individuals and parents or legal guardians of eligible individuals about qualified ABLE programs offered by other states to which Utah residents may apply.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(3): This chapter may not be interpreted to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(3)(a): authorize or provide a disability-related service to an eligible individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(3)(b): be a factor in establishing residency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(3)(c): provide that contributions made into an account are sufficient to cover the qualified disability expenses of an eligible individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(4): An account is not insured or guaranteed by the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-12-201(5): The state does not guarantee the rate or payment of interest or other return on an account.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 13 - Utah State Office of Rehabilitation Act
**************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-101(1): This chapter is known as the "Utah State Office of Rehabilitation Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-101(2): This part is known as "General Provisions."


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(1): "Blind" means an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(1)(a): whose central visual acuity does not exceed 20/200 in the better eye with correcting lenses; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(1)(b): whose visual acuity is accompanied by a limit to the field of vision in the better eye to such a degree that its widest diameter subtends to an angle of no greater than 20 degrees.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(2): "Deaf" means an individual with a diagnosed auditory deficit that renders the individual unable to comprehend spoken language through audition only, even with medical intervention or amplification, and that results in functional limitations in one or more areas of daily living.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(3): "Director" means the director of the Utah State Office of Rehabilitation.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(4): "Disability" means a physical or mental condition which materially limits, contributes to limiting, or, if not corrected, will probably result in materially limiting an individual's activities or functioning.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(5): "Eligible individual" means an individual determined to be eligible to receive services under laws or rules governing eligibility for the program in question.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(6): "Hard of hearing" means an individual with a diagnosed auditory deficit ranging from mild to profound that results in functional limitations in one or more areas of daily living.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(7): "Independent living rehabilitation services" means goods and services reasonably necessary to enable an individual with a severe disability to maintain or increase functional independence.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(8): 35A-1-202 "Office" means the Utah State Office of Rehabilitation created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(9): "Visually impaired" means an individual with a diagnosed impairment of visual function that if not corrected constitutes a material limitation to normal activities or functioning.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-102(10): "Vocational rehabilitation services" means goods and services reasonably necessary to enable an individual with a disability to obtain and retain employment.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103 Office authority.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(1): 35A-1-202 The Utah State Office of Rehabilitation created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(2): The department is the sole state agency designated to administer the state plans for vocational rehabilitation and independent living rehabilitation programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(3): The office is the sole state unit designated to carry out the state plans and other duties assigned by law or the department, including the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(3)(a): determining eligibility for vocational rehabilitation services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(3)(b): providing vocational rehabilitation services to eligible individuals;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(3)(c): determining the types and scope of vocational rehabilitation services provided by the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(3)(d): determining employment outcomes related to vocational rehabilitation services if required; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(3)(e): determining the appropriate uses of federal rehabilitation funding.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(4): (3) The office may not delegate the duties described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-103(5): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-104 Appointment of director -- Administration of the office.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-104(1): The executive director of the department shall appoint the director of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-104(2): The director shall administer the office in accordance with the direction of the executive director and applicable state and federal laws and regulations.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-105 Public funding of vocational rehabilitation and independent living rehabilitation services.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-105(1): Public funding of vocational rehabilitation and independent living rehabilitation services provided under this chapter may only be provided to eligible individuals.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-105(2): The director shall establish priorities for use in determining services to be provided to eligible individuals under this chapter if the demand for services exceeds available funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-105(3): Rights established under this chapter are not transferable or assignable.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-106 Personally identifiable information -- Nondisclosure -- Penalty.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-106(1): Personally identifiable information obtained by the office, its employees, or agents concerning individuals applying for or receiving services under this chapter may not be disclosed without the prior written consent of the individual or the individual's legal representative, except as required for administration of programs or services under this chapter, or as otherwise authorized by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-106(2): Unauthorized disclosure of personally identifiable information obtained under this chapter, or use of such information for unauthorized purposes, is a class B misdemeanor.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-107 Acceptance and use of gifts -- Not subject to appropriation.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-107(1): The director may, with the approval of the executive director, accept and use a gift to the office made unconditionally by will or otherwise for carrying out the purposes of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-107(2): A gift to the office made under conditions that the executive director finds to be consistent with this chapter may be accepted and used in accordance with the conditions of the gift.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-107(3): A gift to the office as described in this section is not subject to appropriation by the Legislature.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-108 Delegation of duties and responsibilities of the office.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The director may, in accordance with applicable law and regulations and with the consent of the executive director, organize the office and assign duties and responsibilities to the office's employees to enable the office to better serve individuals with disabilities and to increase the efficiency and effectiveness of operations.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-109 Office duties to individuals with disabilities.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
In administering this chapter, the office:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-109(1): shall ensure that individuals with disabilities are assisted, so far as reasonably possible, to take their rightful place in open society as independent and self-supporting individuals; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-109(2): may not assist or support any activity that results in unnecessary continuation of a dependent or isolated state or unnecessarily separates individuals with disabilities from open society.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-201 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as "Office Responsibilities."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202 Functions of the office.
---------------------------------------------------------
The office may:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(1): apply for, receive, administer, and distribute funds made available through programs of federal, state, or local governments;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(2): cooperate with federal, state, or local governmental entities to administer programs and program funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(3): contract or cooperate with public or private entities or individuals;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(4): as designated by the responsible authority, and with the approval of the department, perform any functions or services for the federal or state government that relate to individuals with  disabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(5): establish subordinate administrative units necessary to increase efficiency and improve the delivery of services to individuals with disabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(6): establish and operate community service centers, rehabilitation facilities, and workshops, and make grants to public and nonprofit organizations for those purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(7): determine eligibility for, and the nature and scope of, services to be provided under the state plan for vocational rehabilitation or other programs administered by the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(8): Title 55, Chapter 5, Blind Persons Operating Vending Stands - Food Services; Title 55, Chapter 5a, Blind Products Sales assist individuals with severe disabilities to establish and operate vending machine services and other small businesses, and perform services authorized under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(9): furnish materials, tools, equipment, initial stocks and supplies, and occupational licenses needed by rehabilitation facilities, workshops, and small businesses established under this chapter, and develop and execute marketing plans for materials produced by those operations;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(10): place money received by the office through sale of products or services as authorized under this chapter into a fund managed by the office and used to support additional training, production, and sales activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(11): conduct studies and investigations, give demonstrations and make reports, and provide training and instruction related to the work of the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(12): establish and maintain research fellowships and traineeships, including necessary stipends and allowances for those receiving training and instruction;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(13): institute and supervise programs to encourage the conservation of sight and hearing and assist in overcoming and preventing disabling conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(14): provide diagnostic, placement, vocational rehabilitation, training, adjustment, and independent living services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-202(15): do all other things necessary to carry out assignments made by law or the department in assisting and rehabilitating individuals with disabilities.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203 Employment first emphasis on the provision of services.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(1): When providing services to an individual with a disability under this chapter, the office shall, within funds appropriated by the Legislature and in accordance with the requirements of federal and state law, give priority to providing services that assist the individual in obtaining and retaining meaningful and gainful employment that enables the individual to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(1)(a): purchase goods and services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(1)(b): establish self-sufficiency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(1)(c): exercise economic control of the individual's life.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2): (1); (1) The office shall develop a written plan to implement the policy described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(a): assessing the strengths and needs of an individual with a disability;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(b): customizing strength-based approaches to obtaining employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(c): setting expectations, providing appropriate services toward, and recognizing success in:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(c)(i): integrated employment in the workplace at competitive wages and benefits; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(c)(ii): self-employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(d): developing partnerships with potential employers;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(e): providing appropriate employment training opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(f): coordinating services with other government agencies and community resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(g): (1) to the extent possible, eliminating practices and policies that interfere with the policy described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(2)(h): arranging for alternative work experience leading to competitive, integrated employment, including work-based training, volunteer work, and internships.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(3): (1); (2); (2) The office shall, on an annual basis:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(3)(a): (1); (2) set goals to implement the policy described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(3)(b): determine whether the goals for the previous year have been met; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-203(3)(c): (2) modify the plan described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-303 State Rehabilitation Advisory Council.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-303(1): The executive director shall appoint a state rehabilitation advisory council to advise the office and the department  concerning the needs of individuals with disabilities and the provision of vocational rehabilitation services.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-303(2): A majority of the membership of the advisory council shall consist of individuals with disabilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-303(3): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member of the council may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-402 The Division of Services for the Blind and Visually Impaired.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-402(1): There is created as a program within the office the Division of Services for the Blind and Visually Impaired.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-402(2): The director, with the approval of the executive director and after consultation with members of the community to be served by the division, shall appoint an assistant director to administer the services provided by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-402(3): The assistant director shall administer the division in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-402(3)(a): the direction of the director and the executive director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-402(3)(b): applicable state and federal laws and regulations.

-------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-403(1)(a): a business enterprise program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-403(1)(b): workshops, employment, and training; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-403(1)(c): vocational rehabilitation, training and adjustment, sight conservation, prevention of blindness, low vision lenses, and recreational services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-403(2): establish and operate community service centers, rehabilitation facilities, and workshops; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-403(3): perform other duties assigned by the director or the executive director.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-404(2): At least one-half of the members of the council shall be individuals who are blind or have visual impairments.

---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-601(1): This part is known as the "Interpreter Services for the Deaf and Hard of Hearing Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-601(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act All rules made under this part shall be made in accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-602 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-602(1): 35A-13-603 "Advisory board" or "board" means the Interpreter Certification Board created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-602(2): 35A-13-502 "Assistant director" means the assistant director who administers the program called the Division of Services for the Deaf and Hard of Hearing created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-602(3): "Certified interpreter" means an individual who is certified as meeting the certification requirements of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-602(4): "Interpreter services" means services that facilitate effective communication between a hearing individual and an individual who is deaf or hard of hearing through American Sign Language or a language system or code that is modeled after American Sign Language, in whole or in part, or is in any way derived from American Sign Language.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603 Board.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(1): There is created to assist the director of the office the Interpreter Certification Board consisting of the following 11 members:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(1)(a): a designee of the assistant director;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(1)(b): a designee of the Utah Board of Higher Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(1)(c): a designee of the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(1)(d): four professional interpreters, recommended by the assistant director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(1)(e): four individuals who are deaf or hard of hearing, recommended by the assistant director.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(2): (1)(d); (e)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(2)(a): The director shall make all appointments to the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(2)(b): (1)(d); (e) In making appointments under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(3): (1); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(3)(a): Board members shall serve three-year terms, except that for the initial terms of board members, three shall serve one-year terms, four shall serve two-year terms, and four shall serve three-year terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(3)(b): An individual may not serve more than two three-year consecutive terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(3)(c): (1); (2) If a vacancy occurs on the board for a reason other than the expiration of a term, the director shall appoint a replacement for the remainder of the term in accordance with Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(4): The director may remove a board member for cause, which may include misconduct, incompetence, or neglect of duty.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(5): The board shall annually elect a chair and vice chair from among its members.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(6): The board shall meet as often as necessary to accomplish the purposes of this part, but not less than quarterly.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-603(7): 63A-3-107; 63A-3-107 A member of the board may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive travel expenses in accordance with:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604 Powers and duties of the board.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(1): The board shall function as an advisory board to the director and under the director's direction shall perform the following duties concerning the certification of interpreters:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(1)(a): make recommendations to the director regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(1)(a)(i): appropriate rules;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(1)(a)(ii): policy and budgetary matters;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(1)(a)(iii): the appropriate passing score for applicant examinations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(1)(a)(iv): standards of supervision for individuals in training to become certified interpreters;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(1)(b): screen applicants for certification and make written recommendations to the director regarding certification, renewal, reinstatement, and recertification actions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(1)(c): act as the presiding officer in conducting hearings associated with adjudicative proceedings and in issuing recommended orders as designated by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(2): The director, with the collaboration and assistance of the advisory board, shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(2)(a): prescribe certification qualifications;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(2)(b): prescribe rules governing applications for certification;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(2)(c): provide for a fair and impartial method for the examination of applicants;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(2)(d): define unprofessional conduct, by rule, to supplement the definition under this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(2)(e): establish conditions for reinstatement and renewal of certification.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(3)(a): The advisory board shall designate one of its members on a permanent or rotating basis to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(3)(a)(i): assist the director in reviewing complaints involving the unlawful or unprofessional conduct of a certified interpreter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(3)(a)(ii): advise the director when investigating complaints.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-604(3)(b): (3)(a) An advisory board member who has, under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-607 Certification term -- Expiration -- Renewal.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-607(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-607(1)(a): The director shall issue each certificate under this part in accordance with a three-year renewal cycle established by rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-607(1)(b): The director may by rule extend or shorten a renewal cycle by as much as one year to stagger the renewal cycles it administers.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-607(2): 35A-13-604(2) At the time of renewal, the certified interpreter must show satisfactory evidence of compliance with renewal conditions established by the director in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-607(3): Each certificate automatically expires on the expiration date shown on the certificate unless the certified interpreter renews it in accordance with the conditions prescribed by the director.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-608(1)(a): As a condition for renewal of certification, each certified interpreter shall, during each three-year certification cycle or other cycle defined by rule, complete a number of hours of qualified continuing professional education in accordance with standards defined by rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-608(1)(b): The director shall determine the number of hours based upon recommendations from the advisory board.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-608(2): 35A-13-607; (1) If the renewal cycle is extended or shortened under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609 Exemptions from certification -- Temporary or restricted certification.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(1): The following individuals may engage in the practice of a certified interpreter, subject to the stated circumstances and limitations, without being certified under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(1)(a): an individual serving in or employed by the Armed Forces of the United States, the United States Public Health Service, the United States Department of Veterans Affairs, or other federal agency and who is engaged in activities regulated under this part as a part of the individual's service or employment with that federal agency, if the individual holds a valid certificate or license to provide interpreter services issued by another state or jurisdiction recognized by the director;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(1)(b): a student engaged in providing interpreter services while in training in a recognized school approved by the director to the extent the student's activities are supervised by qualified faculty, staff, or a designee, and the services are a defined part of the training program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(1)(c): an individual engaged in an internship, residency, apprenticeship, or on-the-job training program approved by the director while under the supervision of a qualified individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(1)(d): an individual residing in another state and certified or licensed to provide interpreter services in that state, who is called in for a consultation by an individual certified to provide interpreter services in this state, and the services provided are limited to that consultation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(1)(e): an individual who is invited by a recognized school, association, or other body approved by the director to conduct a lecture, clinic, or demonstration on interpreter services, if the individual does not establish a place of business or regularly engage in the practice of providing interpreter services in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(1)(f): an individual licensed in another state or country who is in this state temporarily to attend to the needs of an athletic team or group, except that the individual may only attend to the needs of the team or group and individuals who travel with the team or group, not including spectators; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(1)(g): an individual who is providing interpreter services for a religious entity, to the extent that the religious entity is specifically exempted from liability under federal law.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(2): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(2)(a): (1) An individual temporarily in this state who is exempted from certification under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(2)(b): Violation of any limitation imposed by this section is grounds for removal of exempt status, denial of certification, or another disciplinary proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(3)(a): Upon the declaration of a national, state, or local emergency, the director, in collaboration with the advisory board, may suspend the requirements for permanent or temporary certification of individuals who are certified or licensed in another state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(3)(b): (3)(a) Individuals exempt under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(4): The director, after consulting with the advisory board, may adopt rules for the issuance of temporary or restricted certifications if their issuance is necessary to or justified by:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(4)(a): a lack of necessary available interpretive services in any area or community of the state, if the lack of services might be reasonably considered to materially jeopardize compliance with state or federal law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-609(4)(b): a need to first observe an applicant for certification in a monitored or supervised practice of providing interpretive services before a decision is made by the board either to grant or deny the applicant a regular certification.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610 Grounds for denial of certification -- Disciplinary proceedings.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(1): The director shall refuse to issue a certificate to an applicant and shall refuse to renew or shall revoke, suspend, restrict, place on probation, or otherwise act upon the certificate of a certified interpreter who does not meet the qualifications for certification under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(2): The director may refuse to issue a certificate to an applicant, refuse to renew a certificate, revoke, suspend, restrict, or place on probation the certificate of a certified interpreter, issue a public or private reprimand to a certified interpreter, and issue a cease and desist order in any of the following circumstances:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(2)(a): the applicant or certified interpreter has engaged in unprofessional conduct as defined in this part or by rule under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(2)(b): the applicant or certified interpreter has engaged in unlawful conduct as defined in this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(2)(c): the applicant or certified interpreter has been determined to be mentally incompetent for any reason by a court of competent jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(2)(d): the applicant or certified interpreter is unable to provide interpretive services with reasonable skill and safety because of illness, drunkenness, excessive use of drugs, narcotics, chemicals, or any other type of material, or as a result of any other mental or physical condition, when the individual's condition demonstrates a threat or potential threat to public health, safety, or welfare.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(3): (1) An individual whose certificate has been suspended, revoked, or restricted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(4): (1) The director may issue cease and desist orders:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(4)(a): (1) to a certified interpreter or applicant who is subject to discipline under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(4)(b): to an individual who engages or represents that the individual is engaged in the profession of a certified interpreter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-610(4)(c): to an individual who otherwise violates this part or rules adopted under this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-611 Unlawful conduct.
--------------------------------------------------
"Unlawful conduct" means conduct by an individual that is defined as unlawful under this part and includes:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-611(1): practicing or engaging in, representing oneself to be practicing or engaging in, or attempting to practice or engage in the profession of a certified interpreter if the individual is:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-611(1)(a): not certified to do so and is not exempted from certification under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-611(1)(b): restricted from doing so by a restricted, suspended, revoked, temporary, probationary, or inactive certification;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-611(2): impersonating another certified interpreter or practicing as a certified interpreter under a false or assumed name, except as permitted by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-611(3): knowingly employing an individual to practice or engage in or attempt to practice or engage in the profession of a certified interpreter, if the employee is not certified to do so under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-611(4): knowingly permitting the individual's authority to engage in the profession of a certified interpreter to be used by another individual, except as permitted by law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-611(5): applying for certification under this part, obtaining certification under this part, or otherwise dealing with the director through the use of fraud, forgery, or intentional deception, misrepresentation, misstatement, or omission.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-612 Unprofessional conduct.
--------------------------------------------------------
"Unprofessional conduct" means conduct by a certified interpreter that is defined as unprofessional conduct under this part or under any rules adopted under this part and includes:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-612(1): violating, or aiding or abetting an individual in violating, any provision of this part, rule adopted under this part, or order regulating certified interpreters;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-612(2): violating, or aiding or abetting an individual in violating, any generally accepted professional or ethical standard applicable to the profession of a certified interpreter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-612(3): physically, mentally, or sexually abusing or exploiting an individual through conduct connected with a certified interpreter's practice under this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-13-613 Penalty for unlawful conduct.
--------------------------------------------------------------
An individual who violates Section

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-201(1)(e)(ii): represents a financial institution that has experience managing a portfolio that meets the requirements of the Community Reinvestment Act, 12 U.S.C. Sec. 2901 et seq.;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-201(1)(f): one member, appointed by the executive director, who has expertise in early childhood education;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-201(1)(g): one member, appointed by the state superintendent, who has expertise in early childhood education;

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-201(1)(i): one member, appointed by the executive director, who owns and operates a licensed child care center located in the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202 Elements of a high quality school readiness program.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1): 63N-20-101 A high quality school readiness program that an eligible LEA or eligible private provider runs shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(a): 63N-20-101 an evidence-based curriculum that is aligned with all of the developmental domains and academic content areas defined in the Utah core standards for preschool that the State Board of Education adopts, and that incorporates:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(a)(i): intentional and differentiated instruction in whole group, small group, and child-directed learning; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(a)(ii): 63N-20-101 intentional instruction in key areas of literacy and numeracy, as determined by the State Board of Education, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(a)(ii)(A): 63N-20-101 is teacher led or through a partnership with a contractor as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(a)(ii)(B): includes specific literacy and numeracy skills, such as phonological awareness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(a)(ii)(C): includes provider monitoring and ongoing professional learning and coaching;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(b): ongoing, focused, and intensive professional development for staff of the school readiness program;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(c): ongoing assessment of a student's educational growth and development that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(c)(i): is aligned to the Utah core standards for preschool that the State Board of Education adopts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(c)(ii): evaluates student progress to inform instruction;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(d): administration of the school readiness assessment to each student;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(e): for a preschool program that an eligible LEA runs, a class size that does not exceed 20 students, with one adult for every 10 students in the class;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(f): ongoing program evaluation and data collection to monitor program goal achievement and implementation of required program components;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(g): family engagement, including ongoing communication between home and school, and parent education opportunities based on each family's circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(h): only lead teachers who, by the lead teacher's second year, obtain at least:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(h)(i): the minimum standard of a child development associate certification; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(h)(ii): an associate or bachelor's degree in an early childhood education related field; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(1)(i): a kindergarten transition plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-202(2): Title 63N, Chapter 20, UPSTART A high quality school readiness program that a home-based educational technology provider runs shall meet the requirements as described in

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401 Requirements for a school readiness program to receive funding through a results-based contract.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(1)(a): "Participating program operator" means an eligible LEA, an eligible private provider, or an eligible home-based educational technology provider, that is a party to a results-based contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(1)(b): "Program" means a school readiness program funded through a results-based contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(2): Part 3, Grants for High Quality School Readiness Programs
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(2)(a): Subject to the requirements of this part, an eligible LEA, an eligible private provider, or an eligible home-based educational technology provider that operates a high quality school readiness program may enter into and receive funding through a results-based contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(2)(b): Part 3, Grants for High Quality School Readiness Programs An eligible LEA, an eligible private provider, or an eligible home-based educational technology provider may not enter into a results-based contract while receiving a grant under
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(3): A participating program operator shall ensure that each student who is enrolled in a classroom, or who uses a home-based educational technology, that is part of a participating program operator's program has a unique student identifier by:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(3)(a): if the participating program operator is an eligible LEA, assigning a unique student identifier to each student enrolled in the classroom; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(3)(b): if the participating program operator is an eligible private provider or eligible home-based technology provider, working with the State Board of Education to assign a unique student identifier to each student enrolled in the classroom or who uses the home-based educational technology.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(4): A participating program operator may not use funds received through a results-based contract to supplant funds for an existing high quality school readiness program, but may use the funds to supplement an existing high quality school readiness program.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(5)(a): If not prohibited by the Elementary and Secondary Education Act of 1965, 20 U.S.C. Secs. 6301-6576, a participating program operator may charge a sliding scale fee, based on household income, to a student enrolled in the participating program operator's program.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(5)(b): A participating program operator may use grants, scholarships, or other money to help fund the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6)(a): A participating program operator that is an eligible LEA may contract with an eligible private provider to provide a high quality school readiness program to a portion of the eligible LEA's eligible students if:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6)(a)(i): the results-based contract specifies the number of students to be served by the eligible private provider; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6)(a)(ii): the eligible private provider meets the requirements described in this section for a participating program operator.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6)(b): An eligible LEA that contracts with an eligible private provider shall provide supportive services to the eligible private provider, which may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6)(b)(i): professional development;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6)(b)(ii): staffing or staff support;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6)(b)(iii): materials; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-15-401(6)(b)(iv): assessments.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 35A - Chapter 16 - Office of Homeless Services
**************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Office of Homeless Services."

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(1): "Collaborative applicant" means the entity designated by a continuum of care to collect and submit data and apply for funds on behalf of the continuum of care, as required by the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(2): "Continuum of care" means a regional or local planning body designated by the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development to coordinate services for individuals experiencing homelessness within an area of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(3): 63J-4-202 "Coordinator" means the state homelessness coordinator appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(4): 35A-16-204 "Executive committee" means the executive committee of the homelessness council described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(5): "Homeless Management Information System" or "HMIS" means an information technology system that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(5)(a): is used to collect client-level data and data on the provision of housing and services to homeless individuals and individuals at risk of homelessness in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(5)(b): meets the requirements of the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(6): 35A-16-203(1)(b) "Homeless services budget" means the comprehensive annual budget and overview of all homeless services available in the state described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(7): 35A-16-204 "Homelessness council" means the Utah Homelessness Council created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(8): "Local homeless council" means a local planning body designated by the steering committee to coordinate services for individuals experiencing homelessness within an area of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(9): "Office" means the Office of Homeless Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(10): 35A-16-206 "Steering committee" means the Utah Homeless Network Steering Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-102(11): 35A-16-203(1)(c) "Strategic plan" means the statewide strategic plan to minimize homelessness in the state described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-201 Office of Homeless Services.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-201(1): 63J-4-202 The Office of Homeless Services is under the direction of the state homelessness coordinator appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-201(2): (3); 35A-1-202 The coordinator shall serve as:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-201(2)(a): an advisor to the governor on homelessness issues; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-201(2)(b): (3); 35A-1-202 subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-201(3): The executive director has administrative oversight over the office.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202 Powers and duties of the office.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(1): The office shall, under the direction of the coordinator:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(1)(a): assist in providing homeless services in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(1)(b): coordinate the provision of homeless services in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(1)(c): manage, with the concurrence of Continuum of Care organizations approved by the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development, a Homeless Management Information System for the state that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(1)(c)(i): shares client-level data between state agencies, local governments, and private organizations that provide services to homeless individuals and families and individuals at risk of homelessness in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(1)(c)(ii): is effective as a case management system;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(1)(c)(iii): except for individuals receiving services who are victims of domestic violence, includes an effective authorization protocol for encouraging individuals who are provided with any homeless services in the state to provide accurate information to providers for inclusion in the HMIS; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(1)(c)(iv): meets the requirements of the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development and other federal requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(2): Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act The office may:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(2)(a): Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-202(2)(b): for any federal program that requires the expenditure of state funds as a condition for participation by the state in a fund, property, or service, with the governor's approval, expend whatever funds are necessary out of the money provided by the Legislature for the use of the office.


Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203 Powers and duties of the coordinator.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1): 35A-16-301; 35A-16-303; 35A-16-402 The coordinator shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(a): coordinate the provision of homeless services in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(b): in cooperation with the homelessness council, develop and maintain a comprehensive annual budget and overview of all homeless services available in the state, which homeless services budget shall receive final approval by the homelessness council;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(c): in cooperation with the homelessness council, create a statewide strategic plan to minimize homelessness in the state, which strategic plan shall receive final approval by the homelessness council;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(d): 35A-16-301; 35A-16-303; 35A-16-402 in cooperation with the homelessness council, oversee funding provided for the provision of homeless services, which funding shall receive final approval by the homelessness council, including funding from the:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(d)(i): 35A-16-301 Pamela Atkinson Homeless Account created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(d)(ii): 35A-16-303 Homeless to Housing Reform Restricted Account created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(d)(iii): 35A-16-402 Homeless Shelter Cities Mitigation Restricted Account created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(e): provide administrative support to and serve as a member of the homelessness council;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(f): at the governor's request, report directly to the governor on issues regarding homelessness in the state and the provision of homeless services in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(1)(g): report directly to the president of the Senate and the speaker of the House of Representatives at least twice each year on issues regarding homelessness in the state and the provision of homeless services in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(2): (1)(b) The coordinator, in cooperation with the homelessness council, shall ensure that the homeless services budget described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(3): (1)(c) The coordinator, in cooperation with the homelessness council, shall ensure that the strategic plan described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(3)(a): outlines specific goals and measurable benchmarks for minimizing homelessness in the state and for coordinating services for individuals experiencing homelessness among all service providers in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(3)(b): identifies best practices and recommends improvements to the provision of services to individuals experiencing homelessness in the state to ensure the services are provided in a safe, cost-effective, and efficient manner;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(3)(c): identifies best practices and recommends improvements in coordinating the delivery of services to the variety of populations experiencing homelessness in the state, including through the use of electronic databases and improved data sharing among all service providers in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(3)(d): identifies gaps and recommends solutions in the delivery of services to the variety of populations experiencing homelessness in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(4): (1)(d) In overseeing funding for the provision of homeless services as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(4)(a): shall prioritize the funding of programs and providers that have a documented history of successfully reducing the number of individuals experiencing homelessness, reducing the time individuals spend experiencing homelessness, moving individuals experiencing homelessness to permanent housing, or reducing the number of individuals who return to experiencing homelessness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(4)(b): except for a program or provider providing services to victims of domestic violence, may not approve funding to a program or provider that does not enter into a written agreement with the office to collect and share HMIS data regarding the provision of services to individuals experiencing homelessness so that the provision of services can be coordinated among state agencies, local governments, and private organizations.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(5): In cooperation with the homelessness council, the coordinator shall update the annual statewide budget and the strategic plan described in this section on an annual basis.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(6): 35A-1-109; 35A-16-301; 35A-16-303; 35A-16-402; 35A-16-602
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(6)(a): 35A-1-109 On or before October 1, the coordinator shall provide a written report to the department for inclusion in the department's annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(6)(b): 35A-16-301; 35A-16-303; 35A-16-402; 35A-16-602 The written report shall include:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-203(6)(b)(iv): 35A-16-301; 35A-16-303; 35A-16-402; 35A-16-602 in coordination with the homelessness council, a complete accounting of the office's disbursement of funds during the previous fiscal year from:

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204 Utah Homelessness Council.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204(1): There is created within the office the Utah Homelessness Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204(2): The homelessness council shall consist of the following members:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204(2)(a): a representative of the public sector with expertise in homelessness issues, appointed by the Legislature;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204(2)(b): a representative of the private sector, appointed by the Utah Impact Partnership or the partnership's successor organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204(2)(c): a representative of the private sector with expertise in homelessness issues, appointed by the governor;

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204(2)(r): a member of the House of Representatives, appointed by the speaker of the House of Representatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204(2)(s): the state superintendent of public instruction or the superintendent's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-204(2)(t): a faith-based leader in the state, appointed by the governor;

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205 Duties of the homelessness council.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
The homelessness council:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(1): 35A-16-203(1)(d) shall provide final approval for:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(1)(a): the homeless services budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(1)(b): the strategic plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(1)(c): 35A-16-203(1)(d) the awarding of funding for the provision of homeless services as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(2): 35A-16-203(1)(d) in cooperation with the coordinator, shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(2)(a): develop and maintain the homeless services budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(2)(b): develop and maintain the strategic plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(2)(c): 35A-16-203(1)(d) review applications and approve funding for the provision of homeless services in the state as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(3): shall review local and regional plans for providing services to individuals experiencing homelessness;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(4): shall cooperate with local homeless councils to:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(4)(a): develop a common agenda and vision for reducing homelessness in each local oversight body's respective region;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(4)(b): as part of the homeless services budget, develop a spending plan that coordinates the funding supplied to local stakeholders; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(4)(c): align local funding to projects that improve outcomes and target specific needs in each community;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(5): shall coordinate gap funding with private entities for providing services to individuals experiencing homelessness;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(6): shall recommend performance and accountability measures for service providers, including the support of collecting consistent and transparent data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(7): 35A-16-203(1)(d) when reviewing and giving final approval for requests as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(7)(a): may only recommend funding if the proposed recipient has a policy to share client-level service information with other entities in accordance with state and federal law to enhance the coordination of services for individuals who are experiencing homelessness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-205(7)(b): shall identify specific targets and benchmarks that align with the strategic plan for each recommended award.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302 Uses of Homeless to Housing Reform Restricted Account.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(1): 35A-16-303 The homelessness council may award ongoing or one-time grants or contracts funded from the Homeless to Housing Reform Restricted Account created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(2): As a condition of receiving money, including any ongoing money, from the restricted account, an entity awarded a grant or contract under this section shall provide detailed and accurate reporting on at least an annual basis to the homelessness council and the coordinator that describes:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(2)(a): how money provided from the restricted account has been spent by the entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(2)(b): the progress towards measurable outcome-based benchmarks agreed to between the entity and the homelessness council before the awarding of the grant or contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3): 35A-16-203; 35A-1-109 In determining the awarding of a grant or contract under this section, the homelessness council and the coordinator shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(a): ensure that the services to be provided through the grant or contract will be provided in a cost-effective manner;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(b): give priority to a project or contract that will include significant additional or matching funds from a private organization, nonprofit organization, or local government entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c): ensure that the project or contract will target the distinct housing needs of one or more at-risk or homeless subpopulations, which may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(i): families with children;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(ii): transitional-aged youth;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(iii): single men or single women;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(iv): veterans;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(v): victims of domestic violence;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(vi): individuals with behavioral health disorders, including mental health or substance use disorders;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(vii): individuals who are medically frail or terminally ill;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(viii): individuals exiting prison or jail; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(c)(ix): individuals who are homeless without shelter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d): consider whether the project will address one or more of the following goals:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(i): diverting homeless or imminently homeless individuals and families from emergency shelters by providing better housing-based solutions;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(ii): meeting the basic needs of homeless individuals and families in crisis;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(iii): providing homeless individuals and families with needed stabilization services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(iv): decreasing the state's homeless rate;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(v): implementing a coordinated entry system with consistent assessment tools to provide appropriate and timely access to services for homeless individuals and families;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(vi): providing access to caseworkers or other individualized support for homeless individuals and families;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(vii): encouraging employment and increased financial stability for individuals and families being diverted from or exiting homelessness;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(viii): creating additional affordable housing for state residents;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(ix): providing services and support to prevent homelessness among at-risk individuals and adults;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(x): providing services and support to prevent homelessness among at-risk children, adolescents, and young adults;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(xi): preventing the reoccurrence of homelessness among individuals and families exiting homelessness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(d)(xii): providing medical respite care for homeless individuals where the homeless individuals can access medical care and other supportive services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(3)(e): 35A-16-203; 35A-1-109 address the needs identified in the strategic plan described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(4): In addition to the other provisions of this section, in determining the awarding of a grant or contract under this section to design, build, create, or renovate a facility that will provide shelter or other resources for the homeless, of the homelessness council, with the concurrence of the coordinator, may consider whether the facility will be:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(4)(a): located near mass transit services;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(4)(b): located in an area that meets or will meet all zoning regulations before a final dispersal of funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(4)(c): safe and welcoming both for individuals using the facility and for members of the surrounding community; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(4)(d): located in an area with access to employment, job training, and positive activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(5): (4) In accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(5)(a): the county executive of a county of the first class on behalf of the county of the first class, if the facility is or will be located in the county of the first class in a location other than Salt Lake City;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(5)(b): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(5)(c): a nonprofit entity approved by the homelessness council, with the concurrence of the coordinator; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(5)(d): a mayor of a municipality on behalf of the municipality where a facility is or will be located.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(6): (6); (6)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(6)(a): (6) If a homeless shelter commits to provide matching funds under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(6)(b): (6) In awarding a grant under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-302(7): The office may expend money from the restricted account to offset actual office and homelessness council expenses related to administering this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(1): 35A-16-402 "Account" means the Homeless Shelter Cities Mitigation Restricted Account created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(2): Part 5, Winter Response Plan Requirements "Authorized provider" means a nonprofit provider of homeless services that is authorized by a third-tier eligible municipality to operate a temporary winter response shelter within the municipality in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(3): "Eligible municipality" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(3)(a): a first-tier eligible municipality;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(3)(b): a second-tier eligible municipality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(3)(c): a third-tier eligible municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act "Eligible services" means any activities or services that mitigate the impacts of the location of an eligible shelter, including direct services, public safety services, and emergency services, as further defined by rule made by the office in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5): 35A-16-501; 35A-16-501; 35A-16-502(6)(a) "Eligible shelter" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(a): for a first-tier eligible municipality, a homeless shelter that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(a)(i): has the capacity to provide temporary shelter to at least 80 individuals per night, as verified by the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(a)(ii): operates year-round; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(a)(iii): is not subject to restrictions that limit the hours, days, weeks, or months of operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(b): for a second-tier municipality, a homeless shelter that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(b)(i): has the capacity to provide temporary shelter to at least 25 individuals per night, as verified by the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(b)(ii): operates year-round; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(b)(iii): is not subject to restrictions that limit the hours, days, weeks, or months of operation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(c): 35A-16-501; 35A-16-501; 35A-16-502(6)(a) for a third-tier eligible municipality, a homeless shelter that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(c)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(c)(i)(A): has the capacity to provide temporary shelter to at least 50 individuals per night, as verified by the office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(c)(i)(B): operates for no less than three months during the period beginning October 1 and ending April 30 of the following year; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(c)(ii): 35A-16-501; 35A-16-501; 35A-16-502(6)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(c)(ii)(A): 35A-16-501 meets the definition of a homeless shelter under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(5)(c)(ii)(B): 35A-16-501; 35A-16-502(6)(a) increases capacity during a winter response period, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(6): 35A-16-404 "First-tier eligible municipality" means a municipality that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(6)(a): is located within a county of the first or second class;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(6)(b): as determined by the office, has or is proposed to have an eligible shelter within the municipality's geographic boundaries within the following fiscal year;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(6)(c): due to the location of an eligible shelter within the municipality's geographic boundaries, requires eligible services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(6)(d): 35A-16-404 is certified as a first-tier eligible municipality in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(7): "Homeless shelter" means a facility that provides or is proposed to provide temporary shelter to individuals experiencing homelessness.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(8): "Municipality" means a city, town, or metro township.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(9): "Public safety services" means law enforcement, emergency medical services, or fire protection.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(10): 35A-16-404 "Second-tier eligible municipality" means a municipality that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(10)(a): is located within a county of the third, fourth, fifth, or sixth class;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(10)(b): as determined by the office, has or is proposed to have an eligible shelter within the municipality's geographic boundaries within the following fiscal year;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(10)(c): due to the location of an eligible shelter within the municipality's geographic boundaries, requires eligible services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(10)(d): 35A-16-404 is certified as a second-tier eligible municipality in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(11): "Third-tier eligible municipality" means a municipality that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(11)(a): as determined by the office, has or is proposed to have an eligible shelter within the municipality's geographic boundaries within the following fiscal year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-401(11)(b): due to the location of an eligible shelter within the municipality's geographic boundaries, requires eligible services.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403 Eligible municipality application process for Homeless Shelter Cities Mitigation Restricted Account funds.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(1): An eligible municipality may apply for account funds to mitigate the impacts of the location of an eligible shelter through the provision of eligible services within the eligible municipality's boundaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2): (2)(b)(ii); (2)(c)(iii); (2)(e); (2); 35A-16-402(4); (2)(e); (2)(g); (2)(g)(ii); (2)(g)(i); Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (2)(f); 35A-16-402(4)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(a): The homelessness council shall set aside time on the agenda of a homelessness council meeting that occurs before the beginning of the next fiscal year to allow an eligible municipality to present a request for account funds for that next fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(b): An eligible municipality may present a request for account funds by:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(b)(i): sending an electronic copy of the request to the homelessness council before the meeting; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(b)(ii): appearing at the meeting to present the request.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(c): (2)(b)(ii) The request described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(c)(i): a proposal outlining the need for eligible services, including a description of each eligible service for which the eligible municipality requests account funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(c)(ii): a description of the eligible municipality's proposed use of account funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(c)(iii): a description of the outcomes that the funding would be used to achieve, including indicators that would be used to measure progress toward the specified outcomes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(c)(iv): the amount of account funds requested.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(d): (2)(c)(iii); (2)(e)
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(d)(i): (2)(c)(iii) On or before September 30, an eligible municipality that received account funds during the previous fiscal year shall file electronically with the homelessness council a report that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(d)(i)(A): a summary of the amount of account funds that the eligible municipality expended and the eligible municipality's specific use of those funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(d)(i)(B): an evaluation of the eligible municipality's effectiveness in using the account funds to address the eligible municipality's needs due to the location of an eligible shelter;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(d)(i)(C): (2)(c)(iii) an evaluation of the eligible municipality's progress regarding the outcomes and indicators described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-403(2)(d)(i)(D): any proposals for improving the eligible municipality's effectiveness in using account funds that the eligible municipality may receive in future fiscal years.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(1): "Applicable county" means a county of the first or second class.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(2): "Applicable local homeless council" means the local homeless council that is responsible for coordinating homeless response within an applicable county.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(3): "Capacity limit" means a limit as to the number of individuals that a homeless shelter may provide overnight shelter to under a conditional use permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(4): 11-51-102 "Chief executive officer" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(5): 10-8-41.6 "Community location" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(8): 35A-16-501.5 "County winter response task force" or "task force" means a task force described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(9): "Homeless shelter" means a facility that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(9)(a): provides temporary shelter to individuals experiencing homelessness;
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(9)(b): operates year-round; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(9)(c): is not subject to restrictions that limit the hours, days, weeks, or months of operation.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(10): "Municipality" means a city, town, or metro township.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(13): "Targeted winter response bed count" means the targeted bed count number for an applicable county during the winter response period, as determined jointly by the applicable local homeless council and the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(14): "Temporary winter response shelter" means a facility that:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(14)(a): provides temporary emergency shelter to individuals experiencing homelessness during a winter response period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(14)(b): does not operate year-round.
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-501(15): "Winter response period" means the period beginning October 15 and ending April 30 of the following year.

Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-601 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-601(1): "COVID-19" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-601(1)(a): severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2; or
Utah Code Annotated § 35A-16-601(1)(b): the disease caused by severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2.
